et met sor la plaie, se apostemes chaus i vient, coton moilliet en oile roset soulement, ou en vin stiptice;	and place on the wound, if small abscesses occur, cotton moistened in rose oil only, or in astringent wine;
et s’il n’i a aposteme chaut, si met sus la plaie, s’elle est fresche a tout son sanc, et elle n’est muee par l’air, poudre, que je dirai un poc ci aprés;	and if there is no hot abscess, then apply to the fresh wound, which has not been exposed to air, the powder that I will mention a little later;
et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucuns oignemens, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the area is inflamed, apply some ointments until it is healed.
Et se li plaie est grans si com de tailleure d’espee et de semblans, et les levres ne se pueent assembler par tentes, si les assemble par cousture, si com je dirai as plaies dou ventre, de la costure.	And if the wound is large like a sword cut and similar, and the edges cannot be brought together by suturing, then join them by stitching, as I will explain for belly wounds, of the suture.
Se li plaie est descoverte de l’os, et pent, et ne tient mais que a un poc, si le cope;	If the wound is exposed bone and is loose, holding only slightly to a small point, cut it away;
puis cure la plaie de medicine, et restoure char dure en leu de cuir, et comande au malaide a mengier grosses viandes, si com testes et froment cuit, ausi com poulz, et semblans choses.	then treat the wound with medication, and restore hard flesh in place of skin, and instruct the patient to eat heavy foods, such as brains and boiled wheat, as well as porridge, and similar things.
Et se tu trueves ou cuir porriture, et il n’aert a l’os, si cope lou porrit tot, et giete fuer, puis le cure;	And if you find the skin is rotten and does not adhere to the bone, cut away all the decayed tissue, then apply heat, and afterwards treat the wound.
et se il ait artere en la plaie ou voine, dont sans cort, et il ne puet estainchier par medicines, si quier l’artere, et se tu la trueves desloie, si la lie d’un fil;	and if there is an artery or vein in the wound that cannot be stopped with medication, seek out the vessel, and if you find it dislodged, tie it off with a thread;
et se ceu ne profite mie, si la cauterize.	And if that does no good, then cauterize it.
Et se ces plaies sont petites et simples, si est li cure legiere:	And if these wounds are small and simple, then the treatment is easy:
et est que tu mettes ens ceste poudre qui soude ainsois que li ars l’ait muee.	and it is that you put in this powder which adheres as the fire has moved it.
Et li maniere de la poudre si est:	And the method of the powder is as follows:
pren encens une partie;	take one part of incense;
sanc de dragon II parties;	dragon's blood two parts;
chalz vive III parties, et le poudre subtilment, et emple la plaie, et l’estraint forment, tant qu’elle s’aerse bien et se joigne a tout son sanc;	living chalk three parts, and finely powder it, and apply it to the wound, and press it firmly until it adheres well and joins with all its blood;
et puis la lie bien, et la laisse sens desliier, s’elle n’enfle;	and then mix the mixture well, and leave it undisturbed if it does not swell;
car on n’oste la madicine tant qu’ele soit sanee.	for one should not remove the medicine until it is healed.
Et aucune fois fait on ceu de chalz soulement, quant on n’ait l’encens ne lou sanc de dragon, mais que li ars n’ait muee la plaie.	And sometimes one does this with charcoal alone, when there is no incense or dragon's blood available, but the burn has peeled off the wound.
Et se li ars ait mueit la plaie, meismement en esteit, si n’i met om mie ceste poudre;	And if the burn has caused the wound to fester, especially in winter, one should not apply this powder.
mais met sus aucuns oignemens digestis, ou poulz de farine d’orge faites d’aigue et de miel, tant qu’ele giete bowe;	but apply some digestible ointments, or a poultice made of oatmeal with water and honey, until it releases pus.
puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	then continue to treat it until it is healed.
Et se li brisure d’os vient avec la plaie, et elle est petite, si l’estrai as pinceures subtilz;	And if the bone fracture comes with the wound and it is small, then extract it with fine forceps;
et je vos dirai ci aprés les brisures dou chief.	And I will tell you hereafter about fractures of the head.
de la plaie dou col	of the wound of the neck
Se plaie vient ou col et elle est simple, si n’a point de difference entre li et celi dou chief, mais se li ners dou col ou li artere est copee.	If the wound is on the neck and it is simple, there is no difference from that of the head, but if the nerve of the neck or the artery is cut.
Se c’est li ners, si n’i a autre engien que laissier la cure, et n’i mettre nulle chose restraignant, car il nuit as ners et les fait retraire;	If it is the nerve, then there is no other treatment but to leave it untreated and not apply anything constricting, for it harms the nerve and causes it to withdraw;
et ne mettre sus la plaie rien froit, car li substance des ners est froide, et li continuation d’aus si est avec le cerveil, qui est li plus haus membres;	and do not apply anything cold to the wound, for the tissue of the nerve is cold, and its continuity extends up to the brain, which is the highest part of the body;
mais soit li medicine souez, si com chalz lavee en aigue douce, et mellee avec oile roset, et cucie lavee ausi en aigue douce, et autres pieres de mine selonc ceste maniere, et oignemens moistes.	but let the medicine be applied warm, such as chalk boiled in sweet water and mixed with rose oil, and copper leaves also boiled in sweet water, and other minerals according to this method, and moist ointments.
Et se li plaie est grans, si la cout et lie de bendes, puis la cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the wound is large, then sew and bind it with bandages, then treat it until it is healed.
Et se les plaies sont parfondes et ele est chevee et pleinne de bowe, si la perce ou plus bas leu;	And if the wounds are deep and it is clogged and full of blood, then pierce at a lower place;
et se li artere est copee, et decorremens de sanc en vient, si la desoivre, et la loie, et la cauterize se mestier est;	and if an artery is cut and bleeding occurs, then stop the flow, tie it off, and cauterize if necessary;
et se li espinee de la gorge est copee, ou li keurs, et li conduiz est gardez, par coi la viande va, si cout le keur sus la cainne de la gorge, et ne touchier la gorge mais la remet selonc sa figure naturel;	and if the windpipe is cut or the throat injured, and the passage through which the food goes is guarded, then sew up the wound on the side of the neck, and do not touch the throat but reset it according to its natural shape;
et puis l’estraint avenanment, et le laisse aucuns jors, puis le cure d’oignemens desechans tant qu’il soit sanez;	and then bind it tightly, and leave it for several days, then treat it with drying ointments until it is healed;
et se li plaie a fait empression en l’os, si la quier;	And if the wound has made an impression on the bone, then probe it;
et s’il i a pieces d’os, si les trai fuers toz se tu pues, et ces que tu ne pues avoir, si laisse tant que li plaie porrisse, et soit desevree et aligie li issue;	And if there are fragments of bone, remove them as forcefully as you can, and leave those that you cannot reach until the wound heals and the discharge is cleared;
et se li plaie est fresche, si poudre sus la poudre que j’ai dit.	And if the wound is fresh, apply the powder that I have mentioned.
Et s’il a en la plaie os et il i a fistule, si la cure ensi com j’ai dit en son chapistre.	And if there is bone in the wound and there is an abscess, treat it as I have said in its chapter.
de la plaie de lance ou de coutel	of a lance or knife wound
Se c’est cop de lance ou de coutel, et li plaie est parfonde, si regarde se de la plaie saut ventositez cant li malaides alainne:	If it is a wound from a lance or knife, and the wound is deep, then check if the wound emits gas when the patient changes position:
saiches adonques que li plaie est mortelz;	then you should know that the wound is fatal;
et s’elle n’est parfonde, et elle est fresche a tout son sanc, si n’i mettre mie a la premiere houre la poudre, ne ne la liier mie por le sanc que ne demorse em parfont, et reviegne au cuer, et ocie lou malaide;	and if it is not deep and the wound is fresh with all its blood, then do not apply the powder at first, nor bind it for the blood that does not stop flowing deeply, as it may return to the heart and kill the patient;
mais i met oignement atractif, et le lie II fois le jor;	but apply an adhesive salve, and change it twice a day;
et se tu n’as oignement, si met en la plaie viel coton por succier fuers la moistor, et fai dormir le malaide sus la plaie III jors, ou IIII, ou plusors;	and if you do not have a salve, place old cotton in the wound to absorb the moisture, and allow the patient to rest on the wound for three days, or four, or more.
si n’i venra mie spasme, ne tremor male de cuer n’estraingnemens d’alainne;	then no spasm will come, nor will there be any heart palpitations or foreign body sensations.
et quant tu vois les bones dispositions, si saiches que li plaie est sauve.	and when you see good signs, then you will know that the wound is safe.
Cure la donques de tentes et d’autres cures, tant qu’il soit sanez;	Treat her with tents and other treatments until she is healthy;
et s’elle ne puet saner, et oevre, adés saiches que il i a fistule;	and if she cannot heal and the condition persists, then you will know that there is a fistula;
si la cure si com on doit.	if the treatment as one ought to do.
Et se li plaie est d’incision d’espee ou de coutel, et elle est simple, ou pis ou au dos, si la cure de ceu qui est devant;	And if the wound is from a sword or knife cut, and it is simple, or worse on the back, then treat that of which one is in front;
s’elle est grans, de cousture;	if it is large, stitch it;
et s’elle est petite, de poudre, et s’elle est empressee en l’os, et en a copeit pieces, si quier la plaie, et les trai fuers s’il sont desevrez;	and if it is small, treat with powder, and if it is pressed against the bone, and in pieces that have been severed, then seek to heal the wound, and the torn tendons if they are separated;
et s’il ne sont desevrez, si laisse porrir la plaie, si aligera li estractions;	and if they are not separated, then let the wound heal on its own, which will ease the extraction;
et des autres plaies as autres membres est li jugemens si com nos avons dit.	and for other wounds to other limbs is the judgment as we have said.
dou derrompement dou ventre	from the rupture of the abdomen
Li derompemens dou ventre est grans et moiens et petis;	The rupture of the abdomen is large, medium, and small;
de la grant plaie saut aucune fois li intestine, ou li ners des intestines, par coi li intromission d’aus;	in the large wound, sometimes the intestines, or the nerves of the intestines, protrude, causing infection;
et li costure est plus malaisie, et aucune fois vaut pis li petite plaie que li grans, por ceu c’on remet plus a poinnes les intestines en, s’on ne les i remet de chaut en chaut;	and the suturing is more difficult, and sometimes a small wound is worse than a large one because when the intestines are pushed back in too soon, they do not stay properly;
por ce que li intestine enflent tantost qu’il sentent le froit, si rentrent plus a poinnes, et por ceu vaut mues li moieinne plaie, por ceu c’on ramoine mues l’intestine a son leu que as autres II.	because the intestines swell immediately when they feel the cold, so they are pushed back in more forcefully, and because of this, a smaller wound is better, since the intestine can be more easily returned to its place than with others.
Et saiches que li routure dou ventre est selonc IIII manieres:	And know that a rupture of the abdomen occurs according to IV manners:
les II costures communes avienent en la costure dou ventre, et li costure des autres plaies dou cors et II autres costures propres sont communes as autres plaies;	the II sides common in the side of the abdomen have, and the sutures of other wounds of the body and II other specific sutures are common to other wounds;
et toutevoie elles sont plus propres avec la costure dou ventre, et je dirai une chescune et declairerai.	and nevertheless they are more proper with the side of the abdomen, and I will say each one and explain them.
Je di que quant li plaie est petite, et aucune chose de l’intestine ist fuer, et griés chose est dou remettre, ceu est par l’une des II manieres:	I say that when the wound is small, and something of the intestine comes out, and it is a difficult thing to replace, this is done by one of the two methods:
ou por la petitece de la plaie, si com nos avons dit, ou por ce que li intestine est enflez por le froit.	either because of the smallness of the wound, as we have said, or because the intestines are swollen due to the cold.
Et quant il est frois, eschaufez lou en teil maniere:	And when it is cold, warm it in such a manner:
moillie une esponge ou I mol drapeil en aigue tede soulement, ou tu cuis en aigue squinant et cipre et spique, et arose l’intestine tant que li enfleure soit ostee;	soak a sponge or fine cloth in warm water only, or boil it in scalding water with citrus and spices, and rinse the intestine until the swelling subsides;
et aucune fois fait ce vins restraingnans, et est muedre que awe soule por desenfler.	and sometimes use wine that is constricting, and it is mashed to help reduce the swelling.
Et quant tu vois l’enfleure departir, si amoiste l’intestine d’aigue ou altee et malves soient cuites, car par ceu est aligie li entree a poc de chose;	And when you see the swelling subside, then moisten the intestine with water in which hawthorn and mallows have been cooked, for this gradually opens up the passage;
et s’il n’i puet entrer, si fent un poc la plaie a l’estrument de coi on cope les emorroydes;	and if it cannot enter, then make a small incision in the wound with the instrument used to cut hemorrhoids;
et li premiere cure est muedre que li taille, que nus n’i doit taillier sens grant necessiteit n’i ait;	And the first treatment is cautious regarding the spine, for one should not cut it without great necessity.
et c’est li estrumens por le fendre:	And this is the instrument for cutting:
si trenche dedens en la corbeure et defuer non, et vez ci la forme:	Cut inward along the curve and not outward, and see here the form:
Et quant li plaie est enlargie, et li intestine saut fuer, si le remet arer selonc la forme naturel en son leu propre, se tu en as pooir, car ce vaut mues.	And when the wound is enlarged, and the intestines jump out, place them back in their natural form in their proper place, if you have the power to do so, for that is better.
Quant li plaie est large, et elle est en la partie desoz lou ventre, si covient que tu faices gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et met ses jambes plus haut que son chief;	When the wound is wide and it is in the part below the abdomen, you should have the patient lie on his back, with his legs higher than his head;
et s’elle est en la partie desoz le ventre, si met le chief et le pis plus haut que les parties desoz, et ausi se li routure dou ventre est en l’une des II parties si met t’entente en ceu que li partie navree soit plus haute que li autre;	And if it is in the part below the abdomen, place the head and feet higher than the affected parts, and similarly, if a rupture of the abdomen is in one of the two parts, raise the injured part higher than the other;
et ensi covient amenistrer ceu que je dis en plaies grans et moienes.	And thus it is necessary to treat those things as I say regarding large and medium wounds.
Es plaies petites met ceu que t’est apparilliet, puis aies entre tes mains I ministre pitous ki teigne toute la routure a sa main, et assemble les levres;	In small wounds, apply what is appropriate for you, then hold the compassionate minister in your hands who covers all the wound with his hand, and bring together the lips.
et c’est la maniere commune de costures, et est que tu preignes une aguille ou plusors, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce de la plaie, puis laisse des le chief de la plaie I doi d’espaice, et i fiche une aguille ou il ait I boin fil fort;	and this is the common method of suturing, and it is that you take one needle or more, according to the quantity of the width of the wound, then leave at the head of the wound some space, and insert a needle where there is strong thread.
et perce les II chiés dou cuir avec les II chiés dou siphac, qui est desoz le cuir dedens, tant que tu la faices percier de celle partie, et assemble les II chief dou siphac les IIII ensamble;	and pierce the two edges of the skin with the two edges of the suture, which is inside the skin, until you make it penetrate from that part, and bring together the two ends of the suture all together;
puis l’estrain d’un fil double entor l’aguille de II pars, puis assemble les II chiés de la plaie avenanment, et puis laisse I doi d’espaice, et i fiche une autre aguille;	Then take the thread doubled around the needle on both sides, then bring together the two edges of the wound, and leave one finger's space, and place another needle there.
puis la lie dou fil si com tu as fait la premiere aguille, et ne cesser de ceu faire selonc ceu que tu as mestier des aguilles, tant que toute li plaie soit restrainte;	Then tie the knot of the thread as you did for the first needle, and continue doing so according to how many needles you need, until the entire wound is sutured.
et soient les aguilles moienes, entre subtilz et grosses, car les aguilles subtilz copent toute la char, et les trop grosses si ne pueent mie bien entrer:	And the needles should be medium-sized, between fine and coarse, because fine needles cut through all the flesh, and too coarse ones cannot enter properly:
por ceu covient qu’elles soient moienes;	Therefore, they should be medium-sized;
et ne covient mie bouter les aguilles trop au defuer de la char et dou cuir, k’elles ne copent et oevrent la plaie devant la soudure;	And it is not appropriate to insert the needles too far from the flesh and skin, as they may cut and damage the wound before suturing;
et puis cope les chiés des aguilles, qu’elles ne blecent lou malaide au dormir, et i met tentes ou drapelz au chiés des aguilles por mues tenir, et les laisse tant que li plaie soit soudee;	and then cover the points of the needles so they do not prick the patient while sleeping, and place tents or cloths over the needle points to keep them in place, and leave them until the wound is healed;
et ceste maniere de costure as aguilles est plus covenauble en petites plaies, car il i soffist une aguille ou II.	and this method of suturing with needles is more suitable for small wounds, because it suffices to use one or two needles.
Li seconde costure si est commune, et est que tu assemble les II chiés dou cuir et les II chiés dou syfac ensamble a une aguille ou il ait I fort fil moien;	The second method of suturing is common, and it involves joining the two sides of the skin and the two sides of the tissue together with one needle or thread that is strong.
et quant tu avras perciez ces chiez toz IIII ensamble, si ramoinne l’aguille a la partie ou tu as encomenciet, en la maniere c’on cout les dras;	and when you have pierced all four sides together, then pull the needle back to the part where you started, in the manner one sews cloth;
et met d’espaice entre chescune costure la grossece d’un menor doi;	and place a space between each seam as thick as one thin thread;
ceste costure sevent li home, et je cousi une plaie c’uns hons avoit ou ventre, qui estoit navrez d’un coutel, et estoit li plaie plus d’une palme de grant, et issoit des intestines bien II palmes de grant, et estoit li plaie enmi le ventre.	This is the stitch that a man used to sew up a wound in someone's abdomen, who had been stabbed by a knife, and the wound was more than one hand breadth wide, and two hand breadths of intestines were protruding, and the wound was in the middle of the belly.
Je li ramenai l’intestine puis k’il ot esteit XXIIII houres fuer, et fut li plaie soudee jusc’a XV jors, et le curai, et fut sanez.	I returned the intestine to its place after it had been outside for twenty-four hours, and the wound was sealed up until fifteen days, and I treated it, and he was well.
Et li mire l’avoient jugiet qu’il morroit, et ce fut miracle;	And the physicians had judged that he would die, and this was a miracle;
et ne le curai mie d’oignement, car je estoie en I leu ou on n’en trovoit point, ne nule medicines;	and I did not treat it with ointment, because I was in a place where none could be found, nor any medicine;
et metoie sens plus sus la plaie coton viel II fois le jor, et le lavoie d’aigue de miel tant qu’il fut sanez.	and I would place fresh cotton on the wound twice a day, and wash it with honey water until it was healed.
Or vos dirai les II propres manieres de cousture:	Now I will tell you the two proper methods of suturing:
pren l’aguille, et la boute des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens;	take the needle, and bring it from the outer part to the inner part;
quant elle a perciet le keur de droit en droit, si lai le chief dou siphac ou cousteit ou tu as bouteit l’aguille, et la fai percier d’autre part des la partie dedens jusc’a celi defuer;	when it has pierced the flesh straight through, seize the head of the thread or suture where you inserted the needle, and have it pierce from the inner part to the outer part;
et li entendemens de ceste costure si est que tu cous ausi com li peletier font les pelz, et que tu laisses une fois le syfac d’une part, et le reprent d’autre, tant que li costure soit toute acomplie.	and the understanding of this suture is that you sew as tailors do with fur, and leave one end out while taking up the other, until the entire suture is completed.
Li seconde maniere de costure, que Galiens dist proprement, si est si com aucun font, qui assemblent les II parties ensamble naturelment, et apploient l’un des chief dou syfac a l’autre chief, en teil maniere:	The second method of suturing, which Galen described properly, is as follows: some people bring together the two parts naturally and join one end of the thread to the other in such a manner:
fiche une aguille ou chief dou mirach prochiene, et fai percier celui leu soulement, et laisse les II chiés dou syfac;	Insert a needle into the nearest part of the navel, and pierce that place only, and leave the two heads of the rib cage;
puis torne l’aguille, et la fai percier des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens, as II chiés dou syfac;	then turn the needle, and pierce from the outer part to the inner part, through the two heads of the rib cage;
puis fai percier l’un et l’autre des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens, en II autres chiés dou mirach que sont on l’autre costeit;	then pierce one and the other from the outer part to the inner part, through two other parts of the navel that are on the other side;
et c’est li muedre maniere de costure et li plus commune.	and this is the most effective method of suturing and the most common.
Galiens si dist ceste parolle, et aucun le tesmoignent, c’on doit coudre le ventre a II aguilles, ou il ait fil en chescune;	Galien says this, and some testify that one should sew the abdomen with two needles, each having thread.
et doit on bouter l’une aguille d’une part, et l’autre d’autre, en la maniere de ces qui cousent corroies;	And one must insert a needle on one side, and another on the other, in the manner of those who sew belts;
et saiches que quant li routure est enmi lou ventre, si est li cousture plus griez que des autres leus dou ventre.	And know that when the rupture is in the middle of the abdomen, the suturing is more difficult than for other parts of the abdomen.
Li jugemens de la plaie si est telz com li jugemens des autres plaies:	The judgment of the wound is such as the judgment of other wounds:
et est que quant tu trueves la plaie fresche a tout son sanc, ainsois que li ars l’ait muee, si remet arer l’intestine, et lou cout;	And it is that when you find the wound fresh with all its blood, as if the arrow had drawn it, then reset the intestine and sew it.
puis met sus la poudre enjanrant char, et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucun oignement que soit present, tant que li plaie bowe;	Then apply powder that heals flesh, and if the arrow has drawn blood, then place any available ointment on it until the wound absorbs it;
et chicent li fil, et soient soudez li sifac, et li mirach;	And bind the thread, and let the suture be sealed, and the wound;
puis cure la plaie si com les autres, tant qu’il soit sanez;	then treat the wound as with others, until it is healed;
et se tu n’as medicines, si met sus, tantost qu’ele comance a giter bowe, coton viel, et le remue II fois le jor tant k’il soit sanez.	and if you do not have medicine, place on it as soon as it begins to discharge pus, old cotton, and change it twice a day until it is healed.
Car tu n’as mestier d’autre medicine en plusors dispositions cant les plaies sont simples;	For you do not need other medicines in many cases where the wounds are simple;
et se tu doutes que li plaie ne faice communiteit as membres principelz, si covient ke tu moilles lainne legiere en oile de tempree chalor, ou en oile roset, et la met entor les angres, et desoz les asselles;	and if you fear that the wound might affect the principal limbs, then it is necessary to moisten soft wool in warm oil or rose oil, and place it around the angles, and under the armpits;
et s’il sent dolor ou porriture en bouelz, et maintes fois avient, si les clisterize de vin noir tede, et meismement se li porriture vient jusc’a l’intestine;	If there is pain or corruption in the bowels, and this often happens, then administer an enema of boiled black wine; especially if the corruption reaches the intestine.
et le perce dedens, et saiches que quant c’est li gros intestines, si est plus legier a saner que li petis.	Pierce it inside, and note that when it is the large intestine, it heals more easily than the small.
Li intestine qui est apelez «jeun» ne puet saner quant il est navrez, et c’est por la planteit des voinnes que i sont, et por la subtiliteit de tout le cors, et l’aprochement de sa nature des ners.	The intestine called "jejunum" cannot heal when it is pierced, and this is due to the smallness of the veins that are there, and the subtlety of the whole body, and the proximity of its nature to the nerves.
Et si li zirbe saut de la plaie, si le remet arrier ausi com l’intestine, tandis qu’il est fres;	And if the spleen jumps out of the wound, put it back as you would with the intestine, while it is still fresh.
et s’il est vielz et devenus vers ou noir, si covient que tu lies le leu qui est noir, que decorremens de sanc n’i viegne, car il i a voinnes et arteres;	And if it is old and has turned black or green, then you must ligate the area that is discolored so that no more blood flows through, as there are veins and arteries there.
puis cope ceu qui est entre le liien, et met les II chiés pendans des la partie desoz la plaie jusque defuer por aligier l’estraction quant li zirbes chiet, et li plaie bowe.	Then cut off what is between the ligament, and suspend the two heads from below the wound up to where the splinters fall, so that the extraction may be easier when the shards drop, and the wound will heal.
de la routure dou boueil	Of the fracture of the eye socket
Quant li intestine est rons, et li plaie est petite, si la puet on restorer en aucuns homes, por ceu que je vis que uns hons fut navrez ou ventre d’une lance;	When the intestines are pierced and the wound is small, it can sometimes be repaired in some people, as I witnessed a man who was stabbed in the abdomen with a lance;
et estoit li plaie au destre de l’estomac, et fut envillie et devint fistule, et en issoit li egestion et li ventositez;	and the wound was on the right side of his stomach, it became infected and turned into a fistula, from which his excretions and gases were expelled;
je i mis cure selonc ceu que je poi, et ne cessai de subtilier tant qu’il fut sanez, et li leus soudez.	I applied treatment according to what I could do, and did not stop from carefully removing debris until he was healed, and the flesh closed.
Et quant je le vis souder, je doutai que li malaides n’eust mal en son ventre;	And when I saw him solder it, I feared the patient would suffer pain in his abdomen;
et il n’i ot point de mal, mais demora en millors dispositions, et menjans et bevans;	and he did not suffer any pain, but remained in better disposition, eating and drinking;
et dirent aucun experimentors que quant il a petite plaie en l’intestine, qu’il doit estre liiez en teil maniere:	and some experienced practitioners say that when there is a small wound in the intestine, it should be treated in such a manner:
pren fremis a grans testes, puis assemble les levres de la plaie, et quant li fremis ait overte la bouche, si la met sus les II levres, si qu’elle estraigne sa bouche sus;	take pieces of thread with large knots, then bring the edges of the wound together, and when the threads have opened the mouth, place them on both sides so that they hold the opening closed;
et puis li cope la teste, et ce se tient si qu’il ne puet desliier, puis met I autre fremit aprés en celle maniere que devant, tant que li plaie soit toute porprise;	and then cut the knot, and it remains in place so that it cannot be loosened, then place another thread in the same manner as before, until the entire wound is secured;
et cout la plaie.	and sew the wound.
Cil chief si s’aerdent en l’intestine, et ne vient nulle nuisance au malaide, et se puet on liier l’intestine d’un fil subtil qui est copez de l’intestine d’une beste, en teil maniere:	If the head is embedded in the intestine and causes no harm to the patient, one can ligature the intestine with a fine thread that is cut from an animal's intestine, in such a manner:
pren le chief de cest fil d’intestine que soit mout descharnez, et puis lie au chief de cest fil I fil de lin subtil tort, puis boute le fil en l’aguille, et en cout l’intestine, et le ramoinne en la routure;	take the end of this intestinal thread that is very clean, and then twist a fine linen thread around it, then put the thread on the needle, and sew the intestine, and tie it in the rupture;
et ceste maniere de costure de fremis nen est fuers que selonc la voie de fiance et d’esperance;	and this method of stitching intestines is no stronger than according to the way of faith and hope;
et se li plaie est grans et large, meismement quant elle est en l’un des grailes intestines, si n’i a engien ne santeit, fuer que subtiliteit.	and if the wound is large and wide, especially when it is in one of the major intestinal areas, there is no healing or health without subtlety.
de fistule ou qu’ele soit	of a fistula wherever it may be located
Saiches que toute plaie ou aposteme, quant il enveillist, si est apelee universement «fistule», et meismement quant elle est chevee et rent bowe.	Know that any wound or abscess, when it comes to a head, is generally called a "fistula," and especially when it is drained and becomes hollow.
Et fistule est selonc la verteit nodation fautree dure et blainche, ou on ne sent dolor, et est ausi chevee com li penne d’un oiseil;	And a fistula is according to truth an abnormal knot hard and white, where one does not feel pain, and it is also threadlike as the feather of a bird;
et aucune fois en saut clere bowe, et autre fois espesse;	and sometimes clear and hollow, and at other times thick;
aucune fois poc, et autre fois assez;	sometimes small, and at other times sufficient;
et je en ai jai parleit en la division des plaies, que toute plaie que n’est sanee, et il n’i a char, ce n’est fuers que par une des VIIII causes:	and I have spoken about this in the section on wounds, that every wound which is not healed and has no flesh grows only because of one of the nine causes:
c’est a savoir, par la petitece dou sanc ou cors;	that is to say, due to the smallness of the blood in the body;
ou por sa malice;	or because of its nature;
ou por ceu qu’il i a char dure dedens, et sus les levres, que n’i laisse naistre char;	For because there is hard flesh within, and on the lips, do not allow new flesh to grow;
ou il i a trop de bowe;	where there is too much swelling;
ou li leus est porris, et li matiere est de male qualiteit;	where the wound is rotten, and the matter is of poor quality;
ou li medicine n’est mie bone en la cure;	where the treatment does not have good medicine;
ou por ceu que li corruption est maniere de pestilence;	for because the corruption is like a pestilence;
ou por la proprieteit en la region est tardive li digestion, et tarde li santeit, et enflee par nature;	for because the property in that region is slow to digest, and delays healing, and swells by nature;
ou il i a voinnes ou os:	where there are veins in the bone:
et j’ai ja mostreit toutes ces causes, et les signes, et les cures de medicines en la division.	and I have already shown all these causes, and the signs, and the remedies of medicine in the division.
Or covient que je te faice a savoir la cure de fistule qui est faite par oevre de mains.	Now I shall inform you of the treatment for a fistula which is done by manual work.
Saiches que fistule avient en tous membres dou cors;	Know that a fistula can occur in all parts of the body;
car il i a fistules que vienent as grans voines, et as arteres, et as ners, ou au syfac, ou a l’intestine, ou a la vessie, ou a aucunes des costes, ou a l’espinee dou dos, ou a aucune jointe des mains ou des piez;	for there are fistulas that come to the large veins, and arteries, and nerves, or to the brain, or to the intestines, or to the bladder, or to some of the ribs, or to the spine of the back, or to any joint of the hands or feet;
et si a teil que vient a la proprieteit dou membre principeil, et as semblans leus.	and some affect the principal part of the limb and similar areas.
Et toutes les fistules que sont de ceste maniere sont de grief sanation, et n’i a fors que labour, et ignorance;	And all fistulas of this nature are difficult to heal, and there is nothing but labor, and ignorance;
et se il i a aucune fistule que ne veigne mie jusc’a leu que j’ai dit, et tu as fiance de la cure, et tu la vues conoistre, si pren une tente d’arain ou de fer, se li fistule est droite, si la quier;	and if there is any fistula that does not reach the place I mentioned, and you have confidence in the treatment, and you wish to know it, then take a tent of brass or iron, if the fistula is straight, then press it;
et se li fistule est torte, si la cerche d’une subtil tente de plonc, car li plons se ploie mues entor la tortuositeit;	and if the fistula is curved, then search with a delicate tent of lead, for lead can bend around the curvature;
et se li fistule a mains pertus et tu ne la pues mie bien cerchier par tentes, si la clisterize par l’un des pertus, car la moistors si cort d’un pertus a autre, et la mundifie;	and if the fistula has multiple openings and you cannot properly search it with tents, then irrigate through one of the openings, for moisture passes quickly from one opening to another, and clean it;
puis la quier saigement a ton pooir, que tu conoisses s’il i a os ou nerf, et est chevee em parfont, et demande bien au malaide de la dolor qu’il sent au presser de ta main, et le leu ou il la sent;	then press it carefully to your best ability so you can determine if there are bones or nerves involved, and inquire thoroughly from the patient about the pain they feel when pressed by your hand, and where they feel it;
et quant tu savras vraiement le leu ou elle est, et s’elle est loing de jointure, ou de nerf, ou d’artere ou de voine, ou en aucuns des leus que je t’ai dit, si la cope selonc ceu que je t’ai dit, et oste fuer la fautreure et les chars corrumpues que sont dedens;	And when you know truly the place where it is, and if it is far from a joint, or nerve, or artery or vein, or in any of the places that I have told you, then cut according to what I have said, and remove the pus and the corrupted flesh that are inside;
et puis la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee, et se li fistule est bien parfonde de droit endroit, si covient que tu copes em parfont, tant com tu pues, puis i met tentes moillies en medicine ague, et les boute jusc’au chief de la fistule, tant que li medicine corrode la superfluiteit qui est demoree au fons;	And then treat it until it is healed, and if the fistula is deep from the right place, you must cut deeply as much as possible, then put strips soaked in bitter medicine into it, and place them up to the top of the fistula, so that the medicine corrodes the excess that remains at the bottom.
et puis i met oignemens enjanrans sainne char, tant qu’il soit sanez;	And then apply healing ointments to heal the flesh until it is healed;
et s’il n’est sanez par ceu, si le cauterize si com nos avons dit, et se li os est corrompus de la fistule, si le cope.	And if he is not well by then, cauterize as we have said, and if the bone is corrupted by the fistula, cut it away.
Se voinne ou ners ne te greve ou membres principelz, si com nos avons dit;	If a vein or nerve does not trouble the principal members as we have said;
et se li os est descovers, et il i a corruption et noiror, si lou reis tant que li corruption soit toute ostee, puis le cure de choses enjanrans char tant qu’il soit sanez;	and if the bone is exposed and there is corruption and blackening, remove it until all the corruption is gone, then treat with substances that promote flesh growth until he is well;
et s’il n’est sanez, et rent bowe si com devant, saiches que tu n’es mie alez jusc’a font:	and if he is not well and the swelling returns as before, know that you have not gone far enough:
si descuevre et quier tant que tu soies au fons, et oste toute la corruption, puis restore le leu;	then expose and search until you reach the depth, remove all the corruption, then restore the area;
et s’il est ensi sanez, c’est bien.	And if he is thus healthy, it is well.
Se ceu non, saiches que la corruption est trop en parfont, que tu n’i pues avenir;	If not, you know that the corruption is too deep for you to reach.
si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier a nature;	there is no other remedy but to leave it to nature;
et s’il i a i petit os corrumput, et tu le pues traire as tenailles, si l’estrai a I estrument covenauble a ceu, et s’il i a maint os, si les trai trestoz, ne n’en laissier nes un;	and if there is any small corrupted bone that you can pull with pincers, then extract it with the appropriate instrument, and if there are many bones, remove them all, do not leave even one.
et se li moistor te fait contraire, et il n’i a error ne paour, si cope et moistor et char, et delivre les os.	and if the moisture hinders you and there is no mistake or fear, cut through both flesh and moisture, and free the bones.
Et se tu ne les pues oster a une houre, si met sus la plaie chose enjanrant porriture, et laisse tant que li leus soit porris entor les os, et adonc si avront plus legierement les os;	And if you cannot remove them in one hour, place on the wound something that promotes putrefaction, and leave it until the flesh around the bones is rotten, and then the bones will come out more easily.
et se c’est uns grans os, si com de jambe ou de cuisse, si reis tant soulement la corruption tant que li noiror soit toute ostee, puis restoure la plaie;	And if it is a large bone, such as of the leg or thigh, cut away the corruption only until all the black matter is removed, then restore the wound;
et s’il en i a grant partie dou corrumput, et vient jusc’a mole de l’os;	And if there is a large part of the corrupted flesh, and it extends to the bone tissue;
si le covient soier et coper tout jusc’a la corruption, et puis le cure tant qu’il soit soudez;	it is necessary to search and cut up to the corruption, and then treat it until it heals;
et je te dirai d’une fistule qui avint I home en sa jambe, si que tu i preignes exemple et aide en ton ovraige.	and I will tell you about a fistula that occurred in a man's leg, so that you may take it as an example and aid in your work.
Il fut I jovencelz entor XXX ans, qui ot une dolor en sa jambe d’une cause que vint dedens le cors, tant que les matieres vinrent a la jambe, et fut enflee d’un gros aposteme, et n’ot point de cause defuer por ovrir;	There was a young man around thirty years old who had pain in his leg due to something that came inside the body, until the matter reached his leg and it swelled with a large abscess, and there was no reason for it to burst on its own to open;
mais li mire par lor folie ovrerent tant sus que li apostemes ovri, et en corroient mout de matieres, et devint fistule, et i vint mout de pertus que tuit gitoient bowe et moistor dou cors;	but the physician, due to their folly, operated excessively on the abscess until much matter was discharged, and it became a fistula, and many openings appeared that all flowed with pus and bodily moisture;
et maint mire i mirent cure entor II ans, et n’i ot nul saige en l’art de mains, tant que je i fui apelez, et vi sa jambe et les medicines dont on le curoit, et ceu que corroit par les pertus a grant cors;	and many physicians treated it for two years, and there was no skilled practitioner in the art of hands until I was called to see it, and I saw his leg and the medicines with which he was being treated, and what flowed out through the openings in large amounts;
et devenoit rouges li cors dou jouvenceil, et avoit color citrine.	and the young man's skin turned red, and he had a yellowish complexion.
Je boutai une tente en l’un de ces pertus, et puis cerchai toz les pertus, et trovai que li uns venoit encontre l’autre de toutes les parties de la jambe.	I pitched a tent in one of these holes, and then searched all the holes, and found that they came together from all parts of the leg.
Je me hastai donques, et copai en l’un des pertus tant que je descovri une partie de l’os, et le trovai corrumput et perciet, et venoit li corruption jusc’a l’os dedens;	I hurried then, and probed into one of the openings until I discovered a part of the bone, which I found corrupted and perforated, and the corruption extended to the inner part of the bone;
je soiai ceu qui m’aparissoit de l’os corrumput, et cuidai qu’il n’i eust autre corruption, fuer que celi que je ostai;	I perceived that which appeared to me of the corrupted bone, and I thought there would be no other corruption, though that which I removed.
et comensai a restourer la plaie de medicines sodans par lonc tens, et ne pot souder;	and I began to treat the wound with internal medicines for a long time, and it could not heal.
et puis rencomensai, et descovri l’os si com devant, et trovai la corruption continuee en l’os, et la soiai, et puis l’ostai, et me penai de souder le leu;	and then I began again, and discovered the bone as before, and found the corruption continuing in the bone, and perceived it, and then removed it, and worked to heal the place.
mais je ne pou tant que je copai entor une palme de l’os, et le traï fuer a tout son mole, puis le restourai de medicines;	but I could not do so until I cut around one palm's width of the bone, and then treated it entirely with medicine.
et il fut sanez et soudez hastanment, et ne covint plus rencomencier l’ovraige fors por la foibleté dou malaide, qui ne pooit soffrir, et por la paour de mort que je avoie de lui.	and he was healed and the wound closed quickly, and there was no need to begin the work again except for the weakness of the patient, who could not endure it, and due to my fear of death for him.
Car por l’evacuation sanglotoit sovent, mais il fut sanez entierement, et nasquit en leu de l’os une char dure, et fut de bone disposition et n’ot point de nuisement ne de contraire dou tout en tout, ne a l’aleir ne a venir.	For often there was an evacuation of blood, but he remained entirely healthy, and in the place of the bone grew a hard tissue, and he had good health and suffered no harm or contraindication whatsoever, neither going nor coming.
Et se li os est brisiez en aucun leu dou cors, si le covient soier en ceste maniere:	And if the bone is broken at any place in the body, it must be treated in this manner:
pren I liien, et l’estrain au chief de l’os qui apert, et comande aucun k’il l’estende en haut;	Take a linen cloth and stretch it over the end of the exposed bone, and instruct someone to hold it up.
et met I autre lien de lainne plus gros dou premier liien, et le lie sus la char qui est desor l’os, et estent le chief, si que tu traies la char corrumpue au desoz, et descuevre la char sus le leu ou tu vues soier, que li soie ne blece la char;	and place another cloth made of wool, thicker than the first cloth, and secure it over the flesh that is around the bone, stretching it so that you draw the corrupted flesh inward, and expose the flesh where you wish to treat it, so that the treatment does not injure the flesh.
et met I tison ou une tauble desoz l’os por mues coper la char corrumpue;	and place a piece of cloth or a tablet under the bone to help remove the corrupted flesh;
et covient tant soier com on puet veoir et sentir la corruption, et soier ancor autre fois.	and treat until one can see and feel that the corruption is gone, treating it again if necessary.
Et se li os est corrumpus, et n’apert mie, et li corruptions est en mileu ou en une partie, si descuevre la char toute;	And if the bone is corrupted, and it does not appear clearly, and the corruption is in the middle or in a part of it, then expose the flesh completely;
puis met I tison desoz, et puis soie des l’une partie a l’autre la corruption, et soit li soieure dou lonc de la corruption I poc, si com nos avons dit;	then place the cautery in the middle, and then spread the corruption from one side to the other, and let the cautery be along the length of the corruption as we have said;
et se li corruptions est en la jointure, si cope la jointure corrumpue, et soie l’os ou elle contient de l’autre part;	and if the corruption is in the joint, then cut out the corrupted joint, and let the bone on the other side be exposed;
et se li corruptions est en la continuation des II jointes, si n’i a autre angien que dou coper;	and if the corruption is between two joints, then there is no other remedy but to cut it out;
et se li corruptions est ou poignil de la main, ou ou poignil dou piet, si est mout fort celle chose, mais toutevoie il covient que tu enquieres celle corrosion, coment elle t’apert;	and if the corruption is in a finger of the hand or foot, it is very serious, but still you must inquire about that corruption, how it appears to you;
et la mundifie en toutes les manieres que tu pues, mais que li voine ou li nerf ne te faicent contraire;	and clean in all ways that you can, but do not let the vein or the nerve oppose you;
et saiches que li incisoire et les soies por coper ces os sont maintes, selonc l’assise des os et l’aparance d’ous, et lor grossece et lor subtiliteit, et lor grandor et lor petitece, et lor duresce;	and know that the incising instruments and saws for cutting these bones are many, according to the arrangement of the bones and their appearance, and their thickness and fineness, and their size and smallness, and their hardness;
et por ceu covient il apareillier a chescune semblance d’ovraige son estrument;	and for that reason it is necessary to prepare each tool for its particular task;
et saiches que l’uevre te moustrera l’estrument dont tu avras mestier, selonc la conissance de cest art, et le tesmoignaige des manieres des maladies;	and know that the task will show you the tool you need, according to the knowledge of this art and the testimony of the ways of diseases;
si porpense l’estrument dont tu as mestier selonc ceu qu’il le covient.	so consider the tool you need according to what is required.
dou feu	of fire
Li chiés porrissent ou par cause dedens, ou par cause defuer;	The head of the joint may become stuck either due to swelling inside or due to moving away.
et quant tu avras medicinee celle corrosion par la cure des medicines, et il ne profitent mie, si covient coper celui membre jusques au leu ou li corrosion vient, si que li malaides eschaipe par ceu de la mort, ou par la malice, qui est plus grans, de la defaute dou membre;	and when you have treated that corruption with medicinal care, and it does not improve, then it is necessary to amputate the limb up to where the corruption comes, so that the patient escapes from this by avoiding death, or from the greater evil of losing the limb;
et li signes si est que li membres devient noir, si qu’il semble qu’il soit ars dou feu, et porrist aprés la noiror, pues va celle corrosions de membre em membre, et prent par tout le cors;	and the signs are that the limb turns black as if it were burned by fire, and after turning black, the corruption spreads from limb to limb and affects the whole body;
si te haste dou coper, et se c’est par la percussion d’aucunes venimouses bestes, si com scorpion de mer et wivre et semblans, se li corrosion est au chief dou doi, si le cope, et ne li doner mie espaice de venir jusc’a la main.	hasten to amputate it, and if this is due to the bite of venomous beasts such as a sea scorpion or viper and similar ones, if the corruption is in the head of the hand, then amputate it, and do not give it space to reach the arm.
Et s’elle vient jusc’a la main, si la cope a la jointe, si que la corrosion ne viegne jusc’a bras;	And if it comes to the hand, cover at the joint so that the corrosion does not reach the arm;
et s’elle vient au bras, si le cope au coute;	And if it comes to the arm, cover at the elbow;
et s’elle passe le coute, c’est li mors, et n’i vaut amenistremens fuers que li quantitez de sa vertut;	and if it passes the elbow, it is fatal, and no remedy will avail beyond the amount of its potency;
et tot ensi fai quant li corrosion vient ou piet:	and do this entirely when the corruption comes to the foot:
s’elle vient en la premiere jointe, si la cope aprés l’autre jointe;	if it reaches the first joint, cover it at the next joint;
et s’elle vient ou piet, si cope tout le piet;	and if it reaches the foot, cover the entire foot;
et s’elle monte en la jambe, si cope a la jointure dou genoil;	and if it ascends to the leg, cover at the knee joint;
et s’elle vient desus le genoil, si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier le malaide a mort;	and if it comes above the knee, there is no other remedy but to let the patient die.
et li maniere dou coper ou dou soier le membre si est que tu le lie desus et desoz, et estende uns menistres l’un des liiens aval, et uns autres ministres l’autre liien amont, et tu dessevre la char qui est entre les II liiens a I spatumile large, tant que li os soit descovers;	and the manner of cutting or sawing the limb is that you tie it above and below, and extend one assistant at one end of the ties downward, and another assistant at the other end upward, and you separate the flesh which is between the two ties by a width of one spatrumile until the bone is exposed;
puis le cope ou soie, et met de chescune part I drapeil de lin, si que li soie ne touche le leu sain, et viegne au malaide autre lesion et aposteme chaus.	then cut or saw it, and place a piece of linen on each side so that the saw does not touch healthy flesh, and cause another injury and abscess to the patient.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient quant tu oevres, si cauterize le leu hastanment, ou tu met sus aucunes poudres restraignans;	And if bleeding occurs while you are working, cauterize the area quickly, or apply some astringent powders;
puis revien a ta medicine tant qu’elle soit acomplie, puis lie le membre navreit d’un liien covenauble, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	Then return to your treatment until it is complete, then bind the injured limb with a suitable bandage, and treat it until it is healed.
et je te conterai k’il avint a I home en som piet:	and I will tell you what happened to the man in his sleep:
il li avint une noiror qui sembloit arsure de feu, et celle corrosion vint premier en son doi dou piet, tant qu’elle porprist tout le piet;	a black corruption occurred that seemed burned by fire, and this corrosion began first on the sole of his foot, spreading to cover the entire foot;
et quant li hons vit la corrosion, si se hasta de coper le piet, et fut sanez;	and when the man saw the corruption, he hastened to cover his foot, and was healed;
et lonc tens aprés li revint li corrosion ou doi de la main, et il vint a moi, et je li mis sus choses repercussives aprés la mundification dou cors, et ne pot cesser li corrosions;	and after a long time, the corruption returned to the sole of his hand, and he came to me, and I applied counteracting substances after purifying his body, but could not stop the corrosion;
et il vot que je li copasse la main, et je ne vou, que je avoie esperance de repercuter la matiere;	and he wishes that I cover his hand, and I do not wish to, as I have hope to repel the matter;
et doutai ausi que se je tailloie sa main, qu’il ne morist, car li vertus de l’ome estoit foible;	and I was also afraid that if I cut his hand, he would die, for the strength of the man was weak;
et il se despera toz, et revint en sa terre, et se hasta de coper sa main, et fut sanez;	and he completely despaired and returned to his home, and hastened to cover his hand, and was healed;
et je n’ai ceu conteit fuers que por ceu c’on faice autreteil, s’on en a mestier.	and I do not have it contented except for the purpose of doing otherwise, if one has need of it.
Aucune fois vient aposteme en leu charnut, et demore si longement qu’il fait grant assemblee de bowe;	Sometimes an abscess comes to the flesh, and remains so long that it causes a great accumulation of pus;
et puis ront et perce, et en saut li bowe, et demoure li leus vuis, ausi com uns vasselz;	and then they cut and pierce, and the bone jumps out, and the flesh remains, just like a vessel;
et li cuir qui est desus est ausi subtilz com I drapelz deliiez, et ne corront mie jusc’a l’os, ne jusc’au nerf, et telz maladie si est apelee «sain», et n’est mie apelee «fistule»;	and the skin that is above is as delicate as fine linen, and does not run down to the bone, nor to the nerve, and such a disease is called "sin" (seam), and it is not called "fistula";
mais s’elle est si alongie qu’elle viegne jusc’a l’os em parfont, si est apelee «fistule»;	but if it extends so far that it reaches the bone in depth, then it is called "fistula";
et li cuire si est que tu cope celui cuir tout entor, et meismement quant il est subtilz, ausi com uns drapelz;	and the skin is such that you should cut around it entirely, and especially when it is delicate, like fine linen;
et ne s’aert mie por sa corruption.	and it does not matter for its corruption.
Et se tu as fiance que li cuirs s’aerde, et li corruption n’est mie en parfont, et li cuir est espés de char, si le cure de clistere ensi:	And if you trust that the skin will harden, and the corruption is not deep, and the skin is thick with flesh, then treat it with an enema thus:
regarde se li seins est grans, et li bowe qui en ist est de puant odor, adonques le clisterize de medicine egiptiaine qui est ensi faite:	Look if the breast is swollen, and the pus that comes from it has a foul odor, then administer an Egyptian enema made thus:
prenez aisil, et oile, et litargire, igalment, et metez cuire en I vassel au feu, tant que li medicine soit rouge, et deviegne ausi espesse com miel;	Take honey, oil, and white vitriol in equal parts, and cook them in a vessel over the fire until the medicine becomes red and as thick as honey;
et puis pren de ceu selonc ta necessiteit, et le font en aigue et en miel, et en clisterize lou sein, et estraint le pertus;	and then take as much as you need, and mix it with water and honey, and use it to administer an enema to the affected area, holding the opening tightly;
et laisse la medicine ens par II houres, puis l’estrai en espreignant;	and leave the medicine on for two hours, then extract it while bandaging;
fai ce mout de fois, tant que li seins soit mondefiiez, et soit ostee li puor;	do this several times until the breast is cleansed, and the pus is removed;
et aucune fois est clisterizeis d’aigue de cendres, quant ceste medicine n’est presens, et est que tu preignes cendres de fust de vigne, et giete aigue desus, puis la coule, et en clisterize, tant que tu saiches que li seins est bien mondez;	and sometimes you should administer an enema of ash water when this medicine is not present; take the ashes of grapevine wood, pour water over them, then strain it and use it for an enema until you know that the breast is thoroughly cleansed;
et se li malaides ne le puet soffrir, ne la medicine egiptiaine ne l’aigue de cendres, si le clisterize d’aigue et de miel ou il ait un poc de litargire broiet;	and if the patient cannot tolerate either the Egyptian medicine or the ash water, then administer an enema of water and honey with a little bit of litharge ground up;
ou tu la clistirize de miel et de vin melleit, que li mielz ait proprieteit de mundifiier et de laver, et li vins fait aerdre le sain;	When you make a clyster of honey and mixed wine, let the honey have the property of cleansing and washing, and the wine causes the flesh to soften;
et quant tu as ce fait, et tu as fiance que li seins est bien mundifiiez, si le clisterize de ceu que fait naistre char en li, et est que tu preignes emplaustre diafinit, et le font avec oile roset et en vin;	and when you have done this, and you trust that the breast is well cleansed, then use a clyster to promote flesh growth there, which involves taking an emollient plaster made with rose oil and in wine;
ou tu le clisterize d’aucunes medicines et d’oignemens, dont j’ai dit les proprietez ou traitier des oignemens;	when you administer enemas and ointments with certain medicines, about which I have spoken regarding the treatment of ointments;
et se li pertus dou sein est petis, et li cainne dou clistere n’i puet entrer, si l’eslarge d’un fer un poc, et met ens une tente de l’oignement egiptiein, ou oignement basilicon, tant k’il soit eslargiez;	and if the opening of the breast is small and the tube of the enema cannot enter, widen it with a tool slightly, and place a tent of Egyptian ointment or basilicon ointment until it is sufficiently widened;
et se li plaie est trop large, si la cout et i laisse tant soulement I leu ou li clistere puisse entrer, et se li pertus que giete bowe est au desus, si le cope ou plus bas leu que i est.	And if the wound is too wide, then sew it up but leave enough space only for the poultice to enter, and if the hole from which blood flows out is above, cut it lower down.
Car quant li bowe est en parfont, si n’i laisse enjanrer char;	For when the bleeding is severe, do not allow flesh to grow back.
et se tu ne pues coper lou sein desoz si com tu vues, si appareille en tel maniere que li bowe corre au plus bas leu que i est, car quant li bowe est parfont, si n’i laisse enjanrer char et se tu ne pues coper lou sein desoz si com tu vues, si apareille en teil maniere:	And if you cannot cut the breast as you wish, then prepare it in such a way that the blood flows to the lowest point, for when bleeding is severe, do not allow flesh to grow back, and if you cannot cut the breast as you wish, then prepare it in this manner:
que li bowe corre legierement aval, et n’i lassier rien de la bowe;	so that the blood flows gently downward, and do not leave any of the blood behind;
et pren medicines consolidatives por mettre sor le sain, et estent sus I drapeil de lin que cuevre tout le sain;	and take consolidating medicines to apply on the wound, and place a bandage of linen that covers the entire wound;
puis cope as forces endroit le pertus dou sein I poc plus large dou premier, pues estent oignement souef sus I autre drapel selonc la quantiteit dou pertus, et le met sus le pertus dou sain por aligier la bowe, et n’oster mie le grant drapeil fuers que aprés maint jor une fois;	then cut in the firm places an opening larger than the first, then apply ointment on another cloth according to the size of the opening, and place it over the wound to lighten the burden, and do not remove the large bandage until after several days once;
et celui qui est sor le pertus dou sein, oste sovent por oster la bowe, et saiches ceu que corra de la bowe, se c’est venin ou poc ou assez, ou digeste, ou indigeste;	and the one over the opening of the wound should be frequently removed to relieve the burden, and clean what flows from the wound, whether it is venomous or not enough or sufficient, or digestible, or undigested;
et pren warde se li patiens sent dolor ou nom, et s’il i a aposteme ou non, et quant ta medicine s’est en teil maniere estendue et tu vois la nature que saut sus le pertus dou sain, si saiches que li seins s’aert ja, et aproche li santez;	and be watchful if the patient feels pain or not, and whether there is an abscess or not, and when your medicine is applied in such a manner and you see nature rising over the wound opening, then clean it as the healing begins, and approach the treatment;
et puis le deslie le matin, ou le tier jor, et quant tu delies la plaie, si chainge I autre drapeil, et renovele l’oignement.	And then untie it in the morning, or on the third day, and when you untie the wound, change the cloth, and renew the ointment.
Et se li seins giete bowe indigeste aprés maint jor, saiches que li seins ne s’aert mie.	And if the stomach throws up undigested food after many days, know that the stomach does not settle.
Et se venins subtilz cort aprés lonc tens, si ne te desperer mie de la santeit, car li santez aproche.	And if subtle poisons affect after a long time, do not despair of recovery, for health is near.
Car il i a homes cui tarde enjanremens de char en ses plaies, et de ces que font le contraire;	For there are people who suffer delayed healing of flesh in their wounds, and those who do the opposite;
et se bowe indigeste saut dou sein aprés maint jor, saiches que li seins ne s’aert mie;	and if undigested food remains in the breast after many days, know that the breast does not recover;
et se li seins tarde d’aerdre, et est porloigniez, si ajoste medicines sechans moistes en substance et seches en vertut, si com oignement diafinit, car il i a grant partie de vitriole, et c’est li derriene medicine;	and if the breast takes too long to heal and is delayed, add drying medicines that are moist in substance but dry in virtue, such as a diaphoretic ointment, for it contains much vitriol, and this is the final medicine;
pren oignement dyafinit, et le font avec oile roset, et l’arose de viel vin igal en substance;	Take a definitive salve, and make it with rose oil, and rinse it with old wine equal in substance;
puis le confit et en use;	then apply it and use it;
et ceu meisme fait mielz cuit engroissiez, quant oignemens dyafinit n’est presens, ou tu pren mirre et aloen et encens, et le broie, et le poudre sus le miel quant il est sor le feu;	and this same method works better when thickened, when a definitive salve is not present, take murrex dye and aloeswood and incense, grind them, and powder them over the honey while it is on the fire;
et puis en glue I drapel, et l’estent sor le sein, et aucune fois i aministre on aristologe longe, et racines de lis celeste, qui est ausi com farine de veces et centoire;	and then apply it to a cloth, and place it over the chest, and sometimes administer long leaves of arisarum and roots of heavenly lily, which are also like flour of fennel and centaury;
et en use de simples ou de compostes:	and use simple or compound remedies:
broie les, et en fai poudre, et met sus le miel que j’ai dit, et en use;	grind them, and make powder, and put on the honey that I have mentioned, and use it;
et se li cure est alongie, et n’est curez par ceste cure, adonc saiches que la corruptions est em parfont, et fait empression en l’os, ou as membres durs, ou as liemens;	and if the wound is prolonged and not healed by this treatment, then know that the corruption is deep, and impresses upon the bone, or affects the hard parts of the body, or the ligaments;
si le cure de la cure de fistule, si com nos avons dit ci devant.	treat the wound as we have said before for a fistula.
de l’aposteme de l’ungle	of the abscess of the nail
Panarice est un aposteme que naist desoz l’ungle dou pouchiet de la main, ou dou piet, ou par aventure naist en autres dois;	Panarisis is an abscess that arises beneath the nail of the finger or toe, or occasionally occurs in other joints;
et quant il est envielliez, et on n’i prent garde, si i vient I aposteme chaus, et corront et giete bowe tant qu’elle corront la racine de l’ungle, et par aventure la corront toute;	and when they are old and no attention is paid to them, the abscess becomes severe, and it spreads and discharges pus until it reaches the root of the nail, and possibly extends throughout;
et vient li corrosions jusc’a l’os, tant qu’il i vient dolor puant, et est li chiés dou doi larges, et est li color fuxe.	And the corrosion reaches to the bone, causing a foul-smelling pain, and the shoulder joint is swollen, and the color is bad.
Quant tu le cures si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie, si covient que tu copes a i. fer toute la superfluiteit qui est demoree de l’ungle, puis cauterize la plaie aprés.	When you treat it as we have said in the section, and the treatment is of no use, then you must cut away all the excess that remains from the nail, then cauterize the wound afterwards.
Li cauteres est mout grans aide se li os est sains, et li ungle est sainne;	The cautery is a great aid if the bone is healthy, and the nail is healthy;
et se li ungle apresse la char ens, et l’encomence a poindre, et la blece, si covient que tu mettes lou rait desoz l’ungle que point la char, et la boute en haut, et cope celi char subtilment et legierement, et met sus le remenant de la char medicines ardans et corrosives por oster tout;	and if the nail adheres to the flesh and begins to suppurate and become inflamed, then you must place a thread under the nail that is piercing the flesh, and lift it up, and cut away the affected flesh carefully and gently, and apply the remaining healthy flesh with burning and corrosive medicines to remove everything;
puis le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	then treat it with ointments until it is healed.
Et se li corrosion est en l’os, si le cope, et trai fuer, car tant com li os corrumpus i est, si ne puet saner;	And if the corruption is in the bone, then cut it out, and treat with force, for as long as the corrupted bone remains, it cannot heal;
et se tu vois le doi corrumpre, si le cope en I des nous si com il est devant dit, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	And if you see the toe corrupted, cut it at the first joint as has been previously said, then treat it until it is healed;
et s’il est ferus, et boutez, et il sent grant dolor, si covient que tu le sainnes premier;	And if it is wounded and penetrated, and he feels great pain, then you must treat it first;
puis cope l’ungle dou spatumile agut en taillant de travers desus, et warde que li taille ne viegne jusc’a la char qui est desoz l’ungle, car li malaides sentiroit trop grant dolor;	Then cut the nail of the spatula sharply across, and be careful not to cut into the flesh beneath the nail, for the patient would feel too much pain;
et s’il avient, si met chose sus qui apaise.	And if it happens, place something on it to soothe.
la dolor dou sourdoit de la main	the pain of the stiffness of the hand
Li dois ajostez qui naist en mains d’aucuns homes par aventure est toz charnus, et par aventure i a teil ou il a osses, et aucune fois i a ungle, et aucun d’aus naissent en la racine de la jointure, ou li naissance est en aucuns nous des dois.	The second bone that is born in the hands of some men is entirely flesh, and sometimes there are bones, and at times it has a nail, and some of them are born at the root of the joint, where the birthplace is in some people's case.
Cil qui naist en aucune nout dou doi ne se muet, et cil qui naist a la jointure dou doi, par aventure se muet;	Those who are born with a deformity of the toe do not move it, and those who are born at the joint of the toe may perhaps move it;
la taille de celui qui est charnus si est legiere, en teil maniere:	The body of the person who is fleshy is so light, in such a manner:
taille le en sa racine d’un large spatumile.	cut it at its root with a broad spatula.
Cil qui naist en la racine de la jointure si est grief a curer:	Those who are born with a condition at the root of the joint are difficult to treat:
si te tien dou coper.	so hold the copper gently.
En celui qui naist ou doit au derrien nout, si covient que tu copes premier la char reondement jusc’a l’os, puis cope l’os a une soie convenable a ceu, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	In the one who is born or should be at the rear end, you must first cut the flesh roundly until the bone, then cut the bone in a single stroke suitable for him, then treat it until it is healed.
Li soudemens que vient as dois ensamble vient par naissance, ou par soudement de plaie, ou par arsure de feu, ou par semblans choses.	The swelling that comes to the two together comes by birth, or by inflammatory reaction of a wound, or by burning with fire, or by similar things.
Si couvient que tu copes celle soudeure, si que li doit repairent selonc lor formes naturelz;	You must cut that solder so that the parts repair according to their natural forms;
puis met entre dous tentes ou drapelz moilliez en oile roset, qu’il ne se soudent;	then place between two cloths or linens soaked in rose oil so that they do not solder;
ou tu met entre dous pieces de plonc subtilz, tant que li leus soit soudez, si com il covient.	or place between two pieces of fine wax until the edges are soldered as is appropriate.
Se soudemens vient a aucun de ses dois avec la paume, si cope celle sodure si com il covient.	If swelling comes to either of the two with the palm, then cut that swelling as it should be done.
des vils	of worms
Vis sont voinnes grosses envoloupees pleines de superfluitez melancoliouses, que vienent em plusors membres dou cors;	The veins are thick, wrapped up, full of melancholic excesses, which come to many parts of the body;
et plus avient en jambes de ces qui vont a piet et qui travaillent et portent, que a autres.	and it happens more in the legs of those who walk and work and carry burdens, than in others.
Il covient donques que tu li aministres aucune fois espurgement de cole, et puis le saine de la basilique.	It is necessary then that you administer an enema at times, and then treat them with basilicon salve.
Li cure de fer si est selonc II manieres:	The treatment with iron is according to two methods:
l’une est c’on les cope, et traie on fuer le sanc noir;	one involves cutting and drawing out the black blood;
et li autre maniere si est que tu lieves la voinne, et la trai toute fuer.	and the other method is that you open the vein and draw all the blood out.
Li taille si est selonc ceste maniere:	The treatment with cautery is according to this method:
arose li premier la jambe d’aigue chaude mout fort, tant que li gros sans soit subtiliiez, puis estrain la jambe dou malaide des desus la cuixe jusc’a la partie desoz le genoil;	First, heat the leg with warm water very strongly until the thick blood becomes thin, then lift the patient's leg from above the thigh down to the part below the knee;
puis cope la voinne en I leu, ou en II ou en III, d’une taille large, puis eslieve et trair fuer le sanc noir a ta main, des l’un chief jusc’a l’autre, tant que tant de sans en isse com li vertus dou malaide puet soffrir;	Then cut the vein in one place or two or three, of a wide size, then lift and draw out the black blood to your hand, from one side to the other, until as much blood comes out as the patient's strength can endure;
et puis la lie, et li comande qu’il se teigne de viandes enjanrant cole noire;	and then tie it up, and instruct him to eat foods including black colicwood;
et recomence l’evacuation et la sainie quant les voinnes sont plainnes, et nuist au malaide.	and repeat the evacuation and bleeding when the veins are full, which harms the patient.
Li alevemens de li est selonc ceste maniere:	The treatment of this condition is as follows:
reis la jambe dou malaide, s’il i a mout de poil, puis le met ou bain, et li arose la jambe d’aigue chaude tant qu’elle deviegne rouge, et enflent les voinnes;	raise the patient's leg, if there is much hair, then place it in a bath, and wash the leg with hot water until it becomes red, and swell the veins;
et se tu n’as point de baing, si le chaufe au feu, et puis le cope endroit la voinne dou lonc au chief dou genoil, ou en la partie desoz a la cheville;	And if you do not have water, heat it by the fire, and then cut straight into the vein on the back of the knee, or in the part above the ankle;
puis aoevre le cuir a l’oncine, et escorche la voinne de chescune part, tant qu’ele apere quant on la sent;	then work the skin to the bone, and strip the vein from each side until it appears when you feel it;
et on la voit rouge et noire, et quant elle entre ou cuir si semble ausi com une corde blainche;	and one sees it red and black, and when it enters the skin it seems like a white cord;
puis boute le rait desoz, tant qu’ele soit alevee dou cuir, et puis la pent a l’oncine legier, puis le cope en I autre leu ensus III dois;	then insert the blade underneath until it is raised from the skin, and then gently cut towards the bone, then make another incision above three fingers;
puis escorche le cuir sus la voinne tant qu’ele apere, puis la lieve au rais, si com tu as fait, et la pent a un autre uncine, si com tu as fait premiers;	then strip the skin over the vein until it appears, then lift with the knife as you did before, and cut towards another bone, as you did previously;
puis cope une autre taille, ou plusors se tu en as mestier, puis la lieve, et la cope au doi dou piet, puis la trai et lieve jusc’a la seconde taille;	Then cut another length, or more if you need them, then lift it, and cut at the joint of the foot, then draw it and lift it up to the second joint;
puis l’estrai de taille en taille, tant qu’elle isse toute fuer, puis la cope;	then extract it joint by joint until it comes out completely, then cut it;
et se tu ne la pues traire et lever, si i boute une aguille a tout I fil fort double, et la lie et la trai, et i boute desoz I rait, et torne ta main d’une part et d’autre, tant qu’il en isse;	and if you cannot draw and lift it, pierce the thread with a strong double needle, pull and draw it, and insert below the cut, and turn your hand from side to side until it comes out;
et garde qu’elle ne cope, car s’elle cope, si ne la puet on traire ne lever, et en vient nuisement au malaide;	and be careful that it does not break, because if it breaks, one cannot draw or lift it, and this causes harm to the patient;
et quant tu l’as toute traite, si met sor le leu de la plaie laine moillie en vin et en oile roset;	and when you have treated it entirely, place wool moistened in wine and rose oil over the wound site;
et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	and treat it until it is healed.
Et se li vis est contraite et torte et envoloupee ensamble, et ele n’est mie droite, si com nos avons dit, si covient que tu la fendes tortement, mais ne la coper mie;	And if the vein is constricted and twisted and wrapped around itself, and it is not straight, as we have said, then you must cut it promptly, but do not sever it;
et la trai si com nos avons devant dit.	and treat it as we have said previously.
Li forme dou fer dont on cope la vis si est corbes, et ne trenche mie, qu’il ne cope la voinne;	The shape of the instrument used to cut the vein is curved, and it does not cut cleanly, so as not to sever the vessel;
et est de grosse corbeure, car s’il estoit subtilz, si coperoit la voine, mais soit gros si com nos avons dit, et ci est li forme:	and it is of large curvature, for if it were fine, it would cut the vessel, but it should be thick as we have said, and here is its shape:
de la voinne civile	of the civil vein
Ceste voinne est enjanree en jambes, en chaudes parties ou il ne naist herbes ne arbre, et en terre ou il n’a point de moistor;	This vein arises in the legs, in warm parts where no herbs or trees grow, and in ground where there is no moisture;
et par aventure naist autre part qu’en jambes, et ceu avient de la porriture que vient desoz le cuir, si com il vient dedens le cors serpens et vers, enjanrez entre cuir et char.	and by chance it may arise in other parts than the legs, and this happens due to the putrefaction that comes from under the skin, as it arises within the body like snakes and worms, arising between the skin and flesh.
Et se li signes de l’encomencement de ceste voinne si est qu’il vient en la jambe une tres grans enflammation, puis se chainge li leus, et comence li voinne fors issir, ausi com une racine d’une plante.	And if the signs of the beginning of this vein are that there comes a very large inflammation in the leg, then the location changes, and the vein begins to come out, like the root of a plant.
Quant li chiés apert, si covient que tu envoloupes entor une piece de plonc des une З et demi jusc’a II З., et la noe, et laisse le plonc pendant a la jambe, et totes les fois qu’il en ist point au defuer, si l’envoloupe entor le plonc, et la nowe;	When the wound is open, it is necessary that you wrap around a piece of linen from one and a half to two fingers' width, tie it, and leave the bandage hanging down the leg, and each time there is any looseness, wrap it around the linen again and tie it.
et s’elle est trop longe, si en cope une partie, et envoloupe le remenant, et ne la coper mie en sa racine, tant qu’elle soit toute issue;	and if it is too long, cut off a part and wrap the remainder, and do not cut it at its root until it has come out completely;
car se tu la copes, si rentre en la char, et fait venir aposteme et porriture ou leu, et male maladie;	For if you cut it, it enters the flesh and causes an abscess and putrefaction in that place, and a bad illness;
por la queil chose il covient qu’elle soit traite poc et poc jusc’a chief, et n’en remaigne rien ou cors;	For which reason it must be treated bit by bit until the end, and nothing should remain in the body;
et est aucune fois ceste voinne quant elle est traite de V paumes de lonc, ou de X, et uns hons vint ja a moi, a cui elle issit de X paumes de long, et quant tu la copes, si boute I rais ou pertus, et la perce jusc’a fons, si que tout en isse;	and sometimes this vein when treated from five palms in length, or ten, and one hand twenty to me, from whom it extends ten palms in length, and when you cut it, it emits a jet or perforation, and pierces right through so that everything comes out;
et soit vuidie li matiere qui est dedens, et amenistre au leu medicines enjanrans porriture aucun jor, puis le cure si com les apostemes.	and let the matter that is inside be emptied, and administer to the place medicines that expel putrefaction for some days, then treat it as you would an abscess.
