et ne se covient mie sainier de ventouse devant le bain ne em bain, mais aprés lou bain une houre ou II;	And it is not appropriate to use cupping before a bath or in a bath, but after the bath for one hour or two;
et ne dorme mie aprés la ventosacion, et covient k’il se warse, quant il se doit ventoser et quant il est ventosez.	And do not let them sleep after cupping, but it is necessary for them to walk around when they should be cupped and when they have been cupped.
Et warde se cil qui se saine est coleriques, et se li sans est trop agus et enflamez;	And be wary if the person who is being bled is choleric, and if the blood is too thick and inflamed;
si covient qu’il preigne choses froides, si com pomes grenates et endives et laitues a l’aisil, et semblans choses;	Then it is necessary for them to take cold things, such as sour apples, endive, and lettuce grown in the shade, and similar items;
et menjuce pucins, et char de chastron, et viandes moistes.	and drink pigeon soup, and eat turtle meat, and moist meats.
Et cil qui a froide complexion, si preigne syrop de miel, et vin odorant moien, qui est entre viel et noveil, et menjuce poc, et menjuce pucins et petis oiselz et pijons;	And he who has a cold constitution should take syrup of honey, and half-old-half-new fragrant wine, and eat broth, and eat young sparrows and small birds and pigeons;
et lou jor qu’il se ventousera, si doit plus boivre que mengier;	and on the day he will be cupped, he should drink more than eat;
et covient doner a aucuns homes aucune fois triaicle ou muscate devant la ventosacion, ou aprés, por conforter les membres principalz;	and it is necessary to give some people occasionally tragacanth or nutmeg before cupping, or after, to comfort the main limbs;
et soit subtiliiez li sans, mais il ne covient mie que cil qui sont chaut le boivent.	and let the drink be subtle, but those who are hot should not drink it.
Les ventouses que sont mises sens ferir sont celles que sont mises sus lou foie, et sus la mice, et podagre, et sus lou ventre et la boude et les rains et la hainche, car cil membre ne soffrent mie ferir sus oulz, et ne le fait on fuer que por atraire sanc de membre em membre, si com nos mettons sus les mameles quant li neis sainne;	The cups that are applied without cutting are those placed on the liver, and on the spleen, and for gout, and on the abdomen and buttocks and thighs and hip, because these limbs do not tolerate being cut, and we only make them bleed to draw blood from one member to another, just as we apply them to the breasts when a woman is nursing;
por oster la viscositeit qui est au membre, si com nos metons ventouses sus le ventre et sus la boude por amenuisier le membre;	To remove the viscosity which is in the member, as we put suction cups on the belly and on the throat to reduce the swelling of the limb;
et oste la dolor, quant il i a opilation ou piere, si oste par sa vertu atractive par aventure l’opilation, ou desaert la piere de son leu;	and remove the pain when there is an obstruction or stone, and by its attractive power it might remove the obstruction, or dislodge the stone from its place;
et ensi fait ele quant on le met sus lou foie et sus la mice quant il i a ventositeit retenue, et ces ventouses sont aministrees vuides por sucier tant soulement;	and in this way it acts when placed upon the liver and spleen when there is retained wind, and these suction cups are administered empty to suck only;
et aucune fois sont aministrees ensamble feu, et aucunes fois plainnes d’aigue tede, si com em maladies dou pleuresin, et en tel maniere c’on emplisse la ventouse d’aigue chaude soule, ou d’aigue ou il ait cuit herbes covenaubles a ceu.	and sometimes they are administered together with fire, and at other times filled with warm water, as in cases of pleurisy, and in such a manner that the suction cup is filled with hot water or with water in which suitable herbs have been boiled.
Li forme de la ventouse aministré a feu si est ci:	The form of the cupping vessel administered with fire is as follows:
Et ait II dois de large et demi palme de parfont, et ait ou costeit entor lou mileu I petit pertus, ausi com por bouter une aguille, et soit d’arain, souef devant si qu’ele ne blece lou malaide au mettre sus lou membre;	And let there be two fingers wide and half a palm long, and at the edge in the middle let there be a small hole, as if to insert a needle, and it should be of iron, smooth so that it does not hurt the patient when placed on the limb;
et ait em mileu une verge de travers d’arain ou de fer, por mettre une chandoile emprise, et en soient et grans et petites selonc les maladies et l’eaige de ces qui les prenent;	and in the middle let there be a crossbar of iron or steel to hold a candle securely, and they should vary in size both large and small according to the illnesses and age of those who use them;
car les ventouses des enfans sont autres que des vielz, et des maigres que des gras.	for suction cups for children are different from those for the elderly, and for thin people than for fat ones.
Et doit on ensi mettre ceste ventouse sus lou membre:	And one should place this suction cup in the following manner on the limb:
empren la chandoile de cire ou I linement, et le met emmi la ventouse au traver de la verge qui est emmi la ventouse, si que li clartez soit au fons de la ventouse qu’elle ne brule le malaide;	Take the candle of wax or linen, and place it inside the suction cup over the shaft that is within the suction cup, so that the flame is at the bottom of the cup that it does not burn the patient;
et puis la met sus lou membre, et tes dois soit sus lou pertus que nos avons dit, si que quant on vuet, si en va li vapor, et oste on la ventouse;	and then place it on the limb, and your two fingers should be over the opening we mentioned, so that when you want to, the steam goes in, and remove the suction cup;
et emprent on le linement si com devant, et le rencomence sovent, se tu as mestier.	and take the linen as before, and do it often, if you need to.
En la ventouse donques qui est aministree em maladie de pleuresin, a tout aigue, n’a point de verge ne de pertus, et n’est amenistree fuer que quant ele est plaine d’aigue, et est mise sus lou membre tant soulement;	In the suction cup used for treating pleurisy, there is no shaft or opening, and it is only applied when it is full of water, and is placed on the limb solely;
et c’est li forme:	and this is the form:
Sansues ne sont amenistrees fuer que en membres ou on ne puet mettre ventouses por lour petitece, si com levres et gencives, et semblans leus;	Sanuous should not be applied except to parts where suction cups cannot be used due to their small size, such as the lips and gums, and similar areas;
et en leus desnuez de char, si com doi ou neis, et autres semblans;	and on parts bare of skin, such as the palms or soles, and other similar areas;
et li qualitez de l’user si est que quant tu trueves sansues que sont en aigues douces nettes sens porreture, si les pren;	and the quality of the application is such that when you find sanuous that are in mild conditions and clean for removal, take them;
et les met une nut en aigue douce, tant qu’elles soient famillouses, et n’aient rien en ventres;	and place one in mild liquid until they become familiar and have nothing in their interiors;
et puis soit sainiez de voinne et de ventouse, puis frote le membre tant k’il soit rouges, et met sus les sansues;	and then cleanse the area with a vein and suction cup, then rub the limb until it is red, and place the sanuous on it;
et quant elles seront plainnes, et cherront, se c’est leu ou on puisse mettre ventouse, se li met, car ce vaut mout aprés.	And when they are full, and fall off, if it is a place where one can apply suction cups, then apply them, for this is very beneficial afterwards.
Se ceu non, si leve le leu d’aisil, et puis d’aigue, mout bien, et puis l’espreint;	If not, then lift the area with ease, and then with water, very well, and then compress it;
et se li leus saine trop aprés lou cors des sansues, si moille I drapel de lin en aigue froide, et met sus, tant que li sans soit estenchiés;	and if the place heals too quickly after the suction, then moisten the cloth of linen in cold water and apply it until the wound is spread out;
et se li sans est multipliez, si met sus vitriole broié, ou gales, et semblans choses, tant qu’il soit estenchiez;	and if the wound is multiplied, then apply ground vitriol, or gallnuts, and similar things until it is spread out;
ou tu met sor le leu moitiez de feves pelees, et les laisse tant qu’elles s’aerdent au leu, si estanchera maintenant;	and you place half of peeled beans on the area, and leave them until they dry out there, it will now be staunched;
et se tu en as de plus mestier, si pren autres sansues.	And if you need more, then take other veins.
Et se les sansues ne se vuellent prendre, si frote le leu de sanc fres, ou tu i fiche une aguille tant que li sans en isse, et puis les met sus, et tantost com elles sentent lou sanc, si s’aerdent;	And if the veins do not wish to be taken, then rub the place of fresh blood where you insert a needle so that the blood comes out, and then put them on, and as soon as they feel the blood, they will harden;
et quant tu vues qu’elles chieent, si poudre sus un poc d’aloen et de seil broiet, ou de cendre, si cherront maintenant.	and when you see that they drip, then sprinkle a bit of aloes and frankincense powder, or ashes, and now they will stop dripping.
Ci comence li livre des brisures	Here begins the book of fractures
Cist chapistres est maintes fois necessaires en l’art de medicine, et est restorement de brisure et de desaluement.	This chapter is often necessary in the art of medicine, and it pertains to the restoration of fractures and dislocations.
Saichiez, chier fil, que li fol mire se gietent de cest chapistre, qu’il ne virent onques nul des anciens livres, ne lettre n’en lurent;	Beware, foolish physician, that they throw themselves into this chapter, having never seen any of the ancient books, nor read any letters in them;
et por ceste cause est estraingie li science en nostre terre, car je n’en trovai onques nul boin;	And for this reason, the art is rare in our land, for I have never found anyone good at it;
et n’en sai nient, fuer que par la science des anciens livres, ou j’ai tant estudiiet que je en ai traite la science, et par experiment, et par l’acostumance de ma vie;	and I know nothing except through the knowledge of ancient books, which I have studied so much that I now understand the art, and by experience, and by the habit of my life;
et je vos ai jai descrit en cest chapistre ceu qui est contenut, et l’ai abregié en la fin, et ai mostreit clerement les formes des estrumens que sont amenistrez, si com j’ai fait en ces II chapistres ci devant.	and I have described for you in this chapter what is contained within it, and I have summarized at the end, and clearly shown the forms of the instruments that are used, as I did in the two preceding chapters.
Il covient donques que nos disons ou prologue de cest livre les sommes de la parole et les chapistres ou li saiges met son entendement, et demore sus la verteit, si que cil qui sont esproveit saichent et aprenent cest art noble, et l’aprenent a autrui.	It is therefore necessary that we say in the prologue of this book the summaries of the speech and the chapters where the wise man puts his understanding, and remains on the truth, so that those who are experienced know and learn this noble art, and teach it to others.
Je dis que quant brisure ou dislocation ou torsions ou quasseure vient a aucun, si covient que tu te hastes de sainier lou malaide d’une part et d’autre, s’aucune chose ne lou te tot, si com foiblece de cors, ou enfes, ou viellars;	I say that when a fracture or dislocation or torsion or sprain occurs to anyone, you must hurry to treat the patient from both sides if nothing prevents it, such as weakness of body, children, or elderly people;
ou se li tens n’est tres chaus, ou trop frois;	when the time is neither too hot, nor too cold;
et menjuce cholz frois, c’est a savoir froides joutes, et char d’oiseil et de chevril, et ne boive point de vin, ne menjuce nules grasses chars, et ne s’emplisse mie trop de viandes qui remplissent les voinnes de sanc, tant que tu n’aies doute d’aposteme chaut, ne d’espandement de matiere au membre;	and eat cold things, that is to say cold broths, and meat of birds and goats, and do not drink wine, nor eat any fatty meats, and do not overfill yourself with foods that fill the veins with blood, until you have no fear of a hot abscess or an outpouring of matter in the limb;
si reviegne li malaides a som premerain governement k’il a useit.	if the patient returns to sleep under primary governance that he has used.
Et quant li os brisiés comence a restourer, si covient que on norrisse le malaide de viandes que font gros norrissement, ou il ait viscositeit, si com froment cuit en aigue, et ris, et testes, et piez, et pance de vaiche, et oefz, et poissons fres, et gros vin, et semblans chose.	And when the broken bones begin to restore themselves, it is necessary to nourish the patient with foods that provide thick nutrition, which are viscous, such as boiled wheat in water, rice, and heads, feet, and belly of fish, and eggs, and fresh fish, and strong wine, and similar things.
Car a teil norrissement se reprent mues et plus tost li brisure.	For such nourishment promotes healing and the fracture heals more quickly.
Et saichiez que li os brisiez des vielz et des decrepites ne se pueent mie bien reprendre ne souder selonc lor nature por la sechor des membres, ne cil ausi qui sont trop tendre, si com os de petis enfans;	And know that the bones broken of old and infirm people cannot be well reset or set according to their nature due to the dryness of their limbs, nor can those who are too tender, such as the bones of small children;
mais n’a cure, ramoinne sus l’os brisiet I gros tenrons qui s’aert et joint le membre ensamble, tant qu’il enforce si com il fut devant;	but do not worry, reset on the broken bone with four fingers that hold and join the limb together, as long as it strengthens as it was before;
et ne li tot point de son oevre, et por ceu le covient norrir de grosses viandes, si com nos avons dit.	and do not restrict him from his work, and for this reason he should be fed rich foods, as we have said.
Et saiches que les briseures sont diverses em maintes manieres.	And know that fractures are diverse in many ways.
Car li brisure dou chief est autre que li brisure dou pis, ou de la jambe, et je vos dirai en cest chapistre toutes manieres de brisure.	For the fracture of the head is different from the fracture of the hip, or of the leg, and I will tell you in this chapter all kinds of fractures.
Car il i a brisure que vait a arvol, et autre en aguisant, si com li taille d’une penne por escrire.	For there is a fracture that goes to the bone, and another in sharpening, like the shaft of a quill for writing.
Et si a brisure avec plaie, et brisure a tout une petite fendure.	And there is a fracture with a wound, and a fracture that is just a small crack.
Et a chescune maniere ait son engien, et son estrument propre en la restauration, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient en son leu;	And each method has its own technique, and its proper instrument in the restoration, according to what the memory brings to mind;
et est conue li brisure de l’os par ceu que li leus est tors, et apert bien par defuer, et sone au presseir de la main;	and a broken bone is known by the fact that the limb is twisted, and it is clearly visible by its deformity, and sounds hollow when pressed with the hand;
et quant il n’i a tortuositeit ne son au tochier, et li malaides ne sent mie grant dolor, se n’i a point de brisure;	and when there is no twisting or sound upon pressing, and the patient does not feel great pain, then there is no break;
mais il puet bien avoir tortuositeit, ou fendure, ou petite brisure.	but it may have a twist, or split, or small fracture.
Si ne covient mie que tu lou mueves a la main, mais met sus medicines que vienent ci aprés, et puis l’estraint maintenant subtilment.	It is not necessary to move it with your hand, but apply the medicines that come next, and then press it now gently.
Et saiches que li brisure que vait en arvol, et sont les II parties desjointes, il les covient maintenant mettre a point igalment, ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne;	And you should know that the fracture that goes through the bone, and where the two parts are separated, they must now be placed equally so that pus does not form between them;
et se apostemes chaulz i vient, si lou laisse aucun jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez;	and if pus forms there, leave it for some days until the abscess is resolved;
puis le met igal au mues que tu pues legierement et saigement, et saiches que li restauration de li est plus legiere que li restaurations de celi ou il ait pieces;	then place it evenly as you can lightly and carefully, and know that the healing of this is easier than the healing where there are pieces;
puis l’estraint, si com il covient ci aprés.	then compress it as is appropriate afterwards.
Et se en l’os a piéces brisies, si l’estent de II pars, se c’est mains ou piet, ou a ta main se c’est uns petis membres, ou a II cordes, ou a une corde et a ta main;	And if there are broken bone pieces, secure them from both sides, whether it is the hand or foot, or use two cords, or one cord and your hand;
et met le membre selonc sa figure natureil, si que quant les parties dou membre brisiet sont desevrees, si ramoinne par toz engiens les additions en lor leus au mues que tu pues, et garde que par ton ovraige ne viegne au malaide lesion ne doulor;	and place the limb according to its natural position, so that when the parts of the broken member are separated, reset all additions in their places as much as you can, and ensure that your work does not cause injury or pain to the patient;
et ajoste bien les II chiés des os selonc les millors formes.	and properly align the two ends of the bone according to the best forms.
Et le sent bien a la main s’il te semble k’il ne soit mie bien:	And check carefully with your hand if it seems to you that it is not right:
si la dresce bellement, et ne l’estraindre mie trop, ne presser si com font cil qui i font venir par lor ovraige aposteme chaut et contraction au membre, si com nos avons veut maintes fois.	if you set it properly, and do not pull too tightly, nor press so as to cause inflammation and contraction of the limb due to their work, as we have seen many times.
Et quant li membres est a point, si chastie bien lou malaide qu’il ne lou mueve, ne en veillant ne en dormant, ne en tornant, ne en autre maniere;	And when the limb is properly set, instruct the patient well not to move it, neither while awake nor asleep, nor in turning, nor in any other manner;
et warde bien que li membres soit si asseurez qu’il ne sente nule dolor.	and ensure that the limb is securely set so that it does not feel any pain.
Car quant il sent nulle dolor, si n’est mie a point, et le covient mettre en teil disposition qu’il ne sent nule dolor;	For when it feels any pain, it is not properly set, and it must be placed in such a position that it does not feel any pain;
et te garde k’il soit mis droitement, que tortuositez n’i veigne quant il iert restorez;	and be careful that it is placed correctly, so that no curvature comes about when it is restored;
et li qualitez dou membre brisiet est selonc ceu que je te dis.	and the condition of the broken limb follows what I tell you.
Saiches que li membre brisiet sont divers em petitece et en grandor et en forme.	Know that broken limbs are diverse in smallness and largeness and in form.
Car il i a petis membres, si com brais et dois et semblans:	For there are small limbs, such as arms and thumbs and similar ones:
si covient envoloupeir drapelz de lin molz et subtilz;	It is necessary to wrap strips of soft and fine linen;
et cil qui sont gros, si com cuixe et jambe:	and for those that are thick, such as the thigh and leg:
si covient envoloupeir d’un liien large et dur, car li larges liiens embraice tout le grant membre, et l’estraint de toutes pars igalment, si qu’il n’i a nule taiche;	it is necessary to wrap with a wide and firm bandage, because the wide bands encircle the entire large limb evenly, so there are no gaps.
puis lie entor estoupes legieres, III tours ou IIII selonc lou membre, et estraint ta main un poc a tout le liien, puis vai au desus de la brisure et l’estraint moins, que la brisure puis esloigne un poc la brisure;	then wrap with light rollers, three or four times around the limb, and press your hand slightly on the entire bandage, then go above the fracture and press less, so that the fracture can be slightly separated.
et mollifie lou liien poc et poc, tant que tu preignes grant partie dou leu sain, puis repren I autre liien, et torne entor derechief sus lou leu brisiet;	and gradually loosen the bandage little by little until you cover a large part of the healthy area, then take another bandage and wrap it again over the fractured area.
puis revai a la partie desoz de la brisure, et l’estraint moienement, ne mie trop fort ne trop molement, si com nos avons dit en la premiere lieure desus;	Then return to the part on the side of the fracture and compress it moderately, neither too strongly nor too weakly, as we have said in the first chapter above;
puis met entre les liiens estoupes de lin ou drapelz, tant qu’il soit toz igalz, puis lie tout par desus I bendeil, et puis met tes esteles bien faites sus, s’il n’i a aposteme ou enfleure.	Then place cotton or cloth strips between the bandages so that they are all even, then wrap everything with a bandage, and then apply your well-made splints if there is no abscess or swelling.
Et s’il i a enfleure ou aposteme, si met sus chose apaisant aposteme chaut, et qui oste l’enfleure, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors;	And if there is swelling or an abscess, apply a hot abscess poultice that reduces the swelling, and leave it like this for several days;
puis estrain sus tes esteles, et soient de moitiet d’une large cainne rese saigement, ou de fust dont on fait les clives, ou de rains de palme, et soient selonc ceste figure:	Then apply bandages over your splints, and let them be about half the width of a palm strip, or made from wood used for cleavers, or from palm ribs, and shape them as follows:
mais il covient que li estele que om met sus la brisure soit un poc plus grosse et plus large que les autres;	but it is necessary that the splint which one places on the fracture be a little larger and wider than the others;
et soit ausi longe com il covient au membre de petitece ou de grandor;	and it should also be as long as is necessary for the limb, whether short or long;
puis estraint sus les esteles ausi com tu as fait a la premiere lieure, puis lie desus un fil avenanment, si com en la premiere lieure sus la briseure;	then secure it over the splints just as you did in the first hour, then wrap with bandages as you did for the fracture in the first hour;
plus estroit est ensus, adés moins;	tighter above, looser below;
et covient que li fil soient moien, ne trop gros ne trop menus, et soient de lin mol;	and the bandages should be of medium thickness, neither too thick nor too thin, and made of soft linen;
car se li fil sont gros, si com j’ai veut des oevres des folz qui font lor lieures des cordes de linement tort, et c’est grant error, car li lieure ne puet estre igal s’il est trop subtilz, et ne covient mie qu’il ait entre chescune estele moins dou doi d’espaice.	for if the bandages are too thick, as I have seen in the work of fools who wrap their bandages with twisted linen cords, and this is a great error, because the wrapping cannot be even if it is too thin, and it is not appropriate that there should be less than two fingers' width between each splint.
Et se li malaides est navrez par les chiés des esteles aprés l’estrignement en leus sains, si met desoz elles estoupes de lin, ou lainne charpie, si qu’il ne se blece.	And if the patient is pierced by the tips of arrows after they are drawn from their wounds, place cotton plugs or linen strips beneath them so they do not pierce further.
Quant li plaie est avec la briseure, et li keurs est rompus, je en dirai la cure ci aprés.	When the wound is with the splinter, and the bone is broken, I will describe the treatment hereafter.
Et saiches qu’il ne covient mie estraindre d’esteles toz les membres brisiez le premier jor.	And you should know that it is not appropriate to extract all the splinters from broken limbs on the first day.
Car quant li membres est grans, se n’i covient mie mettre esteles fuer que aprés V jors ou VII, ou plus selonc ta seurteit d’aposteme chaut sorvenant;	For when the limb is large, one should not apply splints forcefully until after five days or seven, or more according to your judgment of a hot abscess ensuing;
et vez ci la maniere des emplaustres anciiens por restorer brisure, dislocation, et torsion:	and see here the manner of ancient plasters for restoring fractures, dislocations, and twists:
et est que tu pren de la farine que se tient as parois dou molin, et la confis avec abun d’uef, et met ceste confection, ne trop clere ne trop espesse, et en use, et c’est li commune maniere de l’emplaustre restorant la brisure a plusors dispositions, et meismement as femmes et as petis enfans, car il n’est mie ne trop chas ne trop frois.	and take flour that is kept in the mill walls, and mix it abundantly with eggs, and apply this preparation neither too thin nor too thick, and use it, and this is the common manner of a plaster restoring fractures in many positions, especially for women and children, because it is not too hot or too cold.
Autre maniere d’emplastre restorans la brisure et la dislocation et la torsion:	Another manner of plaster for restoring fractures, dislocations, and twists:
pren З abareis et ladani et enule et asefetide et gomme arabique et mugat, ana X З.;	Take honey and labdanum and storax and asafoetida and Arabic gum and mastic, each ten parts.
mirre et aloes, ana V З.;	Take myrrh and aloes, each five parts.
alechil VIIII З.;	Take vinegar of bile nine parts.
et en fai poudre, et les melle avec aubun d’uef;	and make a powder, and mix with the yolk of an egg;
se li complexion de l’ome est chaude, si use de cest emplaustre, car il est de bone composition, et restoure les os brisiés hastanment, et vaut a plusors homes.	If the constitution of the person is hot, use this plaster, for it is well composed, and quickly restores broken bones, and is good for many people.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a torsion:	Another way of making a plaster that is good for sprains:
pren mugat et vismalve, ana X З.;	Take mugwort and wild leek, one handful each;
mirre et aloes, ana VIIII З.;	take myrrh and aloes, nine handfuls each;
acaice VI З.;	take acetite, six handfuls;
bolic armenic X З., et broie bien, et confit avec aigue ou abun d’uef, et l’aministre.	take Armenian bole ten handfuls, and grind well, and mix with water or the yolk of an egg, and administer.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a jointes et as os desevrez de lor leus, et apaise la dolor sorvenant, et le taille usent de l’os, et la briseure:	Another method of poultice for joints and bones out of place, which eases the pain that occurs, and helps heal the use of the bone, and fractures:
pren lainne novele, et la moille en aisil et en oile cuit, et met sus lou leu.	take new wool, and boil it in oil, and apply to the affected area.
Cist emplastres ne restoure mie, mais il est boins por apaisier d’aposteme chaut, et oste proprement les dolors.	This plaster does not heal, but it is good for soothing hot abscesses and properly relieves pain.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre qui restoure les os brisiez:	Another way of applying a plaster to restore broken bones:
pren foilles de figuier seches, et foilles de pavol terrestre, et broie ensamble, et fai emplaustre.	take dried mulberry leaves and terrestrial plantain leaves, and grind them together, then make a plaster.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a la restoration de la brisure de l’os et por amenusier lou remenant de l’aposteme.	Another method of plaster for the restoration of a broken bone and to reduce the remaining abscess.
Pren racine de vismalve, camomille, flors de violettes, farine de veces, de chescune une partie;	Take root of chamomile, flowers of violets, flour of vervain, of each one part;
et broie, et confis avec vin, et se li membres est eschaufez, se le confis avec aigue de coriandre moiste, ou d’aigue, et en use.	and grind it, and mix with wine, and if the limb is heated, mix it with moist coriander water or water, and use it.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre plus fors que li premier, quant aposteme dur vient a la restauration dou membre.	Another way of making an ointment stronger than the first one, when a hard abscess comes to the restoration of the limb.
Pren racines de vismalve, et semence de lin, balauste, mellilote, et sansuce, et flors de violetes et de camomille, de toutes ana une partie;	Take roots of chamomile, seeds of flax, baluster, honey lotus, and saussurea, and flowers of violets and chamomile, of each one part;
et broie, et confit avec aigue de salz, ou aigue douce, ou avec vin, selonc la chalor du membre, et son repos.	and grind, and mix with salt water, or fresh water, or with wine, according to the heat of the limb, and its rest.
Ypocras dist en son livre c’on ne mette sus lou membre brisiet por restorer fuer que cerote fait de cire et d’oile, et nulle autre chose plus, et dist qu’il soit entre dous ne trop molz ne trop durs.	Hippocrates states in his book that one should not place anything on a broken limb to restore strength except for cerotic wax made of wax and oil, and nothing else, and he says it should be neither too hard nor too soft.
Et il semble galien c’on doit mettre sus lou membre brisiet, por restoreir, choses seches un poc chaudes, si com mirre et aloes et encens et semblans choses, si com nos avons dit.	And Galen seems to suggest that for restoring a broken limb, dry and slightly warm things should be applied, such as myrrh, aloes, and incense, and similar items, as we have said.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a lesion et a dolor:	Another way of making an ointment that is good for injuries and pain:
pren mugath et chevolz d’omes decopez, ou pennes d’oiseil, et vismalve, et seil igalment, et les broie, et en fai emplaustre et lou lie.	take mastic and chopped human hairs, or bird feathers, and equal parts of herb vervain, and grind them, and make an ointment and mix it well.
Et puis lou deslie un poc aprés, et pren garde se li malaides ne sent nule dolor, ne ne s’est meus li os de son leu;	And then loosen it a little after, and be careful if the patient does not feel any pain, nor has the bone moved from its place;
si ne lou deslie par mains jors.	do not loosen it by hand for days.
Et se dolor vient au leu, ou prurite, sens repos ou enfleure, si te haste, et le deslie, et oste l’emplaustre maintenant;	And if pain comes to the place, or itching, without rest or swelling, then hurry and loosen it, and remove the plaster now;
et pren drapeil legier, et esponge de mer moiste, et plonge en aigue, et en leve lou leu, tant que li prurite cesse, et soit apaisie li dolor;	and take a light cloth, and a sponge soaked in seawater, and apply it to the area, until the itching stops, and the pain is eased;
puis laisse reposer lou membre une houre, puis met sus lainne seche, moillie en aigue ou en oile roset, et lie sus une nut, tant que tu soies seur d’aposteme chaut;	then let the limb rest for an hour, then apply dry wool soaked in water or rose oil, and bind it with a pad until you are sure of a hot abscess;
et repose li enflammation dou membre, et soit ostee li dolor, puis rencomence la lieure subtil, et un poc d’emplaustre, et ne l’estraindre mie si fort com devant;	and reduce the inflammation of the limb, and relieve the pain, then restart the gentle bandaging, and a little plaster, and do not strain it as strongly as before;
et subtilie tant qu’il soit sanez.	and carefully until he is well.
Et se tu vois que aposteme chaus et roujor et dolor et enfleure sont jai osteit dou tout, et tu as mestier d’emplaustre et de liien, si le rencomence, si com tu a fait premier igalment.	And if you see that the abscess is red and swollen and painful and has pus throughout, and you need to apply a poultice and bandage, then restart as you did first equally.
Et s’il ne vient au membre nient de ceu que nos avons dit, si ne le desliier fuer que aprés III jors ou IIII ou V ou VII;	And if nothing of what we have said comes to the limb, do not dislocate it until after three days or four or five or seven;
et aucune fois le laisse XX jors, selonc ce c’on voit, tant que li briseure s’aert, et aproche li ajostement de la char sus;	and sometimes leave it for twenty days, according to what one sees, until the bone fracture heals, and the joint approaches proper alignment;
adonques lou restraint plus que premier, et li engroisse sa viande, si com j’ai dit devant;	then restrain it more than before, and let the flesh grow, as I said earlier;
et se tu vois lou leu sechier plus que mestier n’est, saiches que norrissemens n’i puet venir;	and if you see the area dry more than necessary, know that no new flesh can come there;
arose lou donques d’aigue chaude tede, toutes les fois que tu lou deslies, et ce soit chescun tier jor, et eslaiche un poc la lieure;	apply warm water compresses, every time you dislocate it, and do this every third day, and loosen the bandage a bit;
par cest ovraige donques cort li norrissemens au membre, et esmende hastanment ceu que font li fol mire, que restourent le membre tortement:	Through this work then, correct the positioning of the limb, and quickly remedy what the foolish doctor does, who resets the limb abruptly:
c’est malvais, et si est ovraiges paourous, et je n’i voi autre chose que dou lassier et de l’ovrer droitement.	It is harmful, and such work is dangerous, and I see nothing else but the need to leave it and perform it correctly.
des diverses manieres de brisure	Of various ways of fractures
Maintes manieres de brisures sont, et diverses figures, et les causes sont destintees;	There are many types of fractures, and diverse shapes, and the causes are distinct;
car il a brisures que sont faites de percussion d’espee, et li colz oste tout l’os jusc’a syfac qui est desoz l’os, si com fait haiche ou fust;	for there are fractures caused by the impact of a sword, and the force removes all the bone up to the surface beneath it, as if splitting wood;
et por ceu est apelee ceste maniere de briseure «haichure».	and for this reason, this type of fracture is called a "splitting" or "chopping.
Ou li espee cope l’os par desus sens percier, et est apelee ceste maniere de brisure «absolue»;	When the sword strikes the bone without piercing it, and this manner of fracture is called "absolute";
et est li plaie de ces II brisures grans ou petite.	and the wound from these two fractures is large or small.
Et s’il i a percussion emboee, ou fendure ou de colz de piere, ou de cheoir sus piere, ou d’autres semblans.	And if there is an embedded impact, or a fissure from falling on stone, or from other similar incidents.
Et s’il a brisure persant, qui aproiche jusc’a la toile qui est desoz l’os, ou elle est sus l’os, et est ceste plaie ou grans ou petite.	And if there is a fracture that approaches the membrane under the bone, or is on the bone, and this wound is either large or small.
Et si a plaie qui est reponue en l’os ausi subtil com uns chevous, et est li fendure petite, et por ceu est apelee ceste brisure «capillaire»;	And there is a wound that is embedded in the bone as fine as a hair, and the crack is small, and for this reason it is called a "capillary" fracture;
et si la plaie qui est faite ou par ferir de piere, ou par cheoir, ou par semblant chose, et fait entrer la piece de l’os aval, et est li leus chevez si com font li chaudelier quant il fierent sus les chaudieres;	and there is a wound caused by being hit by a stone, or by falling, or by similar things, which causes a bone fragment to enter below the skin, and the place becomes bruised as if blacksmiths were hammering on their anvils;
si entre li piere dedens.	and a stone enters inside.
Et ceu avient plus a sous qui ont ou chief moistes os, si com chief d’enfant;	And this happens more often to those who have wet bones at their head, such as an infant's head;
et avient a toutes ces manieres de brisure que pieces menues en sont desevrees si com esteles;	and in all these types of fractures, small pieces become dislodged as if they were loose;
et je em parlerai en son leu.	and I will speak about it in its place.
Et conoissons toutes manieres de briseures par la detraction sus elles, et l’inquisition a tentes, et par la char corrumpue qui est sus.	And we recognize all manners of fractures by the depression on them, and the inquiry with probes, and by the corrupted flesh that is upon them.
Li semblance capillaire est conue par ceu que quant on a descovert l’os, et on frote enche sus, si apert li brisure noire.	The hairline fracture is known by this: when one has exposed the bone and rubbed it, the fracture appears black.
En la cure de la brisure, pren garde as accidens dou malaide, et se tu vois nul malvais accident, si com vomissement de cole, et amission d’entendement, et estension, et paumeson, et fievre ague, et les eulz issir fuer et rougir, et autres semblans em plusors dispositions, si ne puet saner sens doute.	In the treatment of the fracture, be mindful of the patient's symptoms, and if you see any bad signs, such as vomiting bile, loss of consciousness, convulsions, paralysis, intermittent fever, and eyes protruding and reddening, along with other similar conditions in many cases, they cannot heal without doubt.
Et se tu ne vois accident espoantauble, et tu esperes salut, si comence la cure.	And if you do not see any alarming symptoms and hope for recovery, then begin the treatment.
Et quant li navrez vient premier a toi, et c’est en yver, si covient oster l’os devant lou quatorzime jor au mues que tu pues.	And when the wounded person first comes to you, and it is in winter, then you must remove the bone before the fourteenth day from the wound that you can.
Et se c’est en esteit, si te haste d’oster l’os devant lou septime jor, ainsois que li toile desoz l’os soit corrumpue, et vienent li accident que nos avons dit.	And if it is in summer, then hasten to remove the bone before the seventh day, so that the tissue under the bone does not become corrupted, and prevent the accidents we have mentioned.
Et se li brisure de l’os vient jusc’a la toile que cuevre lou cerveil, si covient que tu fendes la partie fendue ensi:	And if the fracture of the bone reaches the tissue that covers the brain, then you must split the broken part as follows:
et est que tu preignes lou chief dou malaide navreit, et descuevre sus l’os en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et sus la figure de la plaie plus souef que tu pues, et se decorrement de sanc vient au descovrir l’os, ou aposteme chaus, se li aide de ceu qu’il covient, et est que tu emplisses lou leu de drapelz moilliez en oile roset;	and it is that you take the patient's head in your hands, and expose the bone in all ways that you can, and around the shape of the wound as deeply as you can, and if blood flows out upon uncovering the bone, or an abscess appears, with the help of what is needed, and it is that you fill the place with cloths soaked in rose oil;
et fai reposer la plaie tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et soies asseurez de decorrement de sanc;	and let the wound rest until the swelling is eased, and be assured of the cessation of blood flow;
puis comence entor l’os a oster, et c’est fait selonc II manieres d’ovraige:	then begin to remove around the bone, and this is done according to two methods of work:
l’une manieres si est que tu copes au taillement estroit devant, et c’est li forme:	one method is that you cut closely around the incision, and this is the form:
Et puis i boute I autre taillement plus grant que lou premier.	And then make the other incision larger than the first one.
Et li seconde maniere si est que tu aies nombre de taillemens divers, les uns estrois et les autres larges, et soient a pointe, et soient de fer inde;	And the second method is that you have various cuts, some narrow and others wide, and they should be sharp, and made of iron;
et en oevre legierement, que tu ne bleces le chief.	and work gently so that you do not injure the head.
Et se li os est fors et durs, si covient que tu lou perces entor, ainsois que tu i aministres taillemens avec tareres, ne mie parfont qu’il ne percent outre l’os dou test, et doit avoir desus la pointe une marge ou I cercle, que ne laisse passer la pointe outre l’os;	And if the bone is hard and protruding, you must pierce around it gently, thus applying cuts with chisels, but not deeply enough to penetrate beyond the skull bone, and it should have a margin or circle above the tip so that it does not allow the point to go beyond the bone;
et t’en covient avoir plusors, si que chescuns viegne en son leu de l’espés de l’os, si que tu aies tareres por toz test;	and you must have several of them so that each comes in its place according to the thickness of the bone, so that you have splinters for all parts of the head;
et c’est li forme des III manieres de tareres:	and this is the form of the three kinds of splinters:
Li qualitez por percier entor l’os brisiet est que tu mettes I tarere sus l’os, et torne a tes dois tant que tu saiches que li os est perciez;	The quality for piercing around the broken bone is that you place one splinter on the bone, and turn it until you know that the bone is pierced;
puis remet lou tarere autre part un poc aprés, et ensi fai tout entor, puis cope as incisoires l’espaice de l’os qui est entre les pertu, et fai ceu plus subtilment que tu pues, et legierement, si com nos avons dit, tant que tu en traies l’os a ta main, ou a aucun des estrumens que tu as si com tenailles, pinceures;	then place the splinter slightly apart elsewhere, and do this all around, then cut into the bone spaces between the holes, and do this more carefully than you can, and gently, as we have said, until you draw out the bone with your hand, or with any of the tools you have such as forceps, pincers;
et garde que tu ne touchier au cerveil ne au syfac.	And make sure you do not touch the brain or the cerebellum.
Et quant tu avras l’os perciet, et trait, si couvient que tu reses l’apreteit qui est demoree de l’os a tout I autre estrument semblant a un incisoire, mais il covient qu’il soit plus tenves et plus subtilz que li autre incisoire;	And when you have pierced the bone and extracted it, then you must close the aperture that remains in the bone with an instrument similar to a lancet, but it must be thinner and finer than other lancets.
et s’il demore rien des petis os, ne nulles escailles, si les oste legierement a I des estrumens;	And if any small bones or fragments remain, remove them gently with the instrument;
puis cure la plaie de tentes et d’oignemens que nos avons dit.	Then treat the wound with dressings and ointments as we have described.
Et li autre maniere d’ovraige si est cil que Galiiens dist, qui est plus saus;	And the other method of work is that which Galen described, which is more skillful;
et le loa molt fort, et c’est sa parole.	And he praises it very much, and this is his speech.
Il covient premier que tu descuevres une partie de l’os, lai ou li brisure apert mues, si que quant tu avras descovert celle partie, si metras desoz lou chief de cest incisoire lenticulaire, de coi ci est li forme:	It is necessary first that you uncover a part of the bone where the fracture has moved out, so that when you have uncovered this part, you place below the head of this chisel, here is its form:
Et ne trenche mie d’une part, et est li partie ague en II costez, si que li trenchans est devers l’os;	And it does not cut from one side, and the part is angled on both sides, so that the cutter faces the bone;
puis fier d’un petit maillet sus, si que tu copes legierement l’os tout entor, et te done bien en garde de la toile que est desoz;	then tap it gently with a small mallet, so that you lightly groove the bone all around, and be very careful of the tissue below;
s’elle est aerse a l’os, si l’oste legierement, car on l’oste bien sens nuisement, et sens paor.	if it is adhered to the bone, remove it gently, for it must be removed without harm, and without fear.
Et se li brisure de l’os ne perce jusc’a la toile, et li os est copez tant soulement par desus, et il i a petites pieces, si couvient rere celle asperiteit, et oster les escailles au raseur subtil dont tu dois avoir diverses quantitez, por amenistrer en chescun leu le plus covenauble, selonc l’ovraige et la figure de la brisure.	And if the bone fracture does not penetrate to the skin, and the bone is broken only from above, with small pieces, then it is necessary behind that roughness, to remove the scales with a fine scraper of which you must have various quantities, to apply in each place the most suitable, according to the work and the shape of the fracture.
Si reis devant de grant raseurs, et aprés de plus subtilz, et ne cesser de ceu faire tant k’il soit bien.	Start with large scrapers and then use finer ones, and do not stop doing this until it is well done.
En chescune des autres tailleures capillaires et brisure subtil, covient que tu amenistres cause selonc son adrecement;	In each of the other hair cuts and fine fractures, you must treat according to their alignment;
et c’est chose que n’est mie reponue a celui qui a mis son estude en cest art.	And this is something that is not answered by one who has devoted his study to this art.
Et se li syfac est descovers, si covient que tu preignes I drapeil de lin, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et le moille en oile roset, et le mete sus la plaie;	And if the wound is exposed, then you should take a piece of linen, according to the size of the wound, and moisten it in rose oil, and place it on the wound;
puis pren I autre drapeil doublé en II ou en III, et le moille en vin et en oile roset, et le met sus le premier drapeil;	then take another piece of linen folded in two or three layers, and moisten it in wine and rose oil, and place it over the first piece of linen;
et fai ceu plus legierement que tu pues, que tu ne grever lou syfac, puis aministre par desus I autre liien, et ne l’estraindre mie fuer que tant k’il teigne la plaie soulement;	and apply it as lightly as you can, so as not to burden the wound, then cover it with another cloth, and do not tighten it more than necessary to just cover the wound;
et le laisse ensi I jor ou II, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, puis le deslie, et i aministre medicines si com racines de lis, et farine de veces, et poudre d’encens, et aristologe, et semblans choses;	and leave it thus for one or two days until the swelling is reduced, then unbind it, and administer medicines such as lily root, flour of oats, powder of incense, arsitolochia, and similar things;
et de ces choses fai poudre, et met sus la plaie, et i aministre adés medicines mondefians sens mordication;	and from these things make powder, and apply it to the wound, and immediately administer cleansing medicines without incision;
et warde que li plaie soit adés nette, que tu n’i laissier mie l’oignement, ne n’i laissier mie assembler bowe, car quant bowe s’asemble sus la toile dou cerveil, si la corront et porrist, et avient au malaide grans malice;	and ensure that the wound is immediately clean, do not leave any ointment on it, nor allow pus to accumulate, because when pus accumulates on the brain's cloth-like tissue, it can cause damage and lead to great harm for the patient;
car quant on met sus lou syfac chose mordant, si nercist par desus.	for when something irritating is applied to the surface, it can cause irritation from above.
Pren warde donques, se nulz mavais accidens vient au malaide, si com nos avons dit, si est doutable sens doute.	Therefore, pay attention if any harmful accident happens to the patient, as we have said, it is doubtful without doubt.
Et se noiror n’i vient fuers que por la medicine c’on a mise sus, que teil vertu ait, si covient que tu preignes une partie de miel, et III parties d’oile roset et en glue I drapel, et lou met sus lou syfac;	And if blackness does not come from anything other than the medicine that you have applied, such power it has, then you must take one part of honey, and three parts of rose oil and mix one drop, and put it on the surface;
puis lou cure de manieres de cures qu’il couvient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	then treat it in the manner of treatments that are necessary until it is healed.
Saiches que aucune fois sont brisies les II parties dou neis desus, ou li une par li soulement, car ce sont II os;	Know that sometimes the two parts of the skull above are broken, or just one part, because these are two bones;
et cil desoz est cartillaginous, et ne brise mie, si ne fait fuer k’enbower ou tordre, et puis saine.	and the one below is made of cartilage and does not break, unless it is bent or twisted, and then it heals.
Et se l’une des II parties est brisie, si covient que tu boutes ton petit doi ou pertus dou neis, et met igal cele brisure dedens a ton doi indice, et au pouchet par defuer, tant que li neis reveigne selonc sa figure natureil;	And if one of the two parts is broken, then you must insert your small finger or probe into the nostril and place the break exactly within your finger, and outside the nostril according to its natural shape, until the nose returns to its original form;
et fai ce legierement, et warde que li malaides ne sente dolor par ton ovraige.	And do this gently, and watch that the patient does not feel pain from your work.
Et se li brisure est en la partie desus lou neis, et ne puet venir li dois au leu, si couvient que tu lou mettes igal au chief d’un rait un poc gros.	And if the break is in the part above the nose, and cannot come to its place, then you must set it equally along a thin rod.
Et se li brisure est de II pars, si refai autretel, et te haste de restorer lou premier jor, se tu pues;	And if the fracture is in two parts, then do likewise, and hurry to restore it on the first day if you can.
se ce non, aprés lou septime ou le disime, quant li apostemes chaus est apaisiez, puis bouthe au chief dou neis tentes de drapelz de lin, se li brisure est en une partie.	unless, after the seventh or tenth day, when the swelling has subsided, then apply to the head of the nose cloths of linen if the fracture is in one part.
Ou tu boutes I autre d’autre part, se li brisure i est;	Where you apply it on another part, if the fracture is there;
et soient les tentes si grosses qu’eles emplissent les pertus dou neis.	and let the cloths be thick enough to fill the openings of the nose.
Et dirent aucun restorour c’on doit moillier les tentes em burre, et muer chescun jor.	And some responders say that the tents should be lubricated with butter, and changed each day.
Il ne me semble mie que ce soit bien, mais covient qu’elles soient moillies en confection d’aubun d’uef, et de poudre de molin;	It does not seem right to me that they should be used as is; they must be moistened in a preparation of egg white and powdered alum.
puis laisse la tente, tant que li os soit fers, et li cartilaiges endurcis.	Then leave the dressing on until the bone is hardened, and the cartilage is firm.
Et aucune fois boute on ou neis pennes d’oie en leu de tentes, et si a I souef drapeil entor, et se tient la briseure, et soffle li malaides parmi;	And sometimes one places goose feathers in place of dressings, and they are covered with a bandage, and the patient blows through them;
or fai lou kel ke tu vues.	do as you see fit;
Et se apostemes chaus vient au neis tandis com tu i oevres, si i met cerote ou coton moilliet en oile roset, ou en I poc de dyaquilon.	And if abscesses come to the nose while you are working on them, apply plaster or cotton moistened in rose oil, or a little piece of myrrh.
Et se apostemes chaus n’i vient, si met emplastre par defuer, de farine de sisament, et de poudre d’encens, confites avec aubun d’uef, puis met sus estoupes legieres, et ne liier mie lou neis;	And if abscesses are slow to come, apply a plaster around it, made of powdered fenugreek and frankincense, mixed with some egg white, then place light cotton on top, and do not tie the nose;
et se li brisure dou neis est petite, et il est brisiés em menues pieces, si l’estrai as estrumens covenables a ceu, puis cout la fendure, et la cure de choses enjanrans char, et soudant, si com emplastres et oignemens covenables a ceu;	and if the nose is fractured in small pieces, remove them with appropriate instruments, then sew up the wound, and treat it with substances that promote flesh growth and healing, such as plasters and suitable ointments;
et s’il n’a dedens lou neis nule plaie, si lou cure de tentes, et i met cainnes de plonc, tant qu’il soit sanez.	and if there is no wound inside the nose, then treat it with tents, and place strips of linen, until he is healed.
de la routure de la mandibule	of the fracture of the jawbone
Quant li mandibule est route desoz, et il n’i a point de plaie defuer, et li brisure est defuer tant soulement, et n’est mie brisiez en dous, fuer que corbelz dedens, si le conoist on legierement.	When the mandible is fractured from below, and there is no wound to surface, and the fracture is only superficial, and it is not broken into two parts, except possibly a small chip inside, one can easily recognize this.
Il covient, se li brisure est en la destre partie, que tu boutes ton doi indice en la bouche dou malaide;	It is necessary, if the fracture is on the right side, that you place your index finger in the patient's mouth;
et se li brisure est en la mandibule senestre, si boute ton doi indice de la main destre, et boute la brisure dedens legierement, et l’afaite a l’autre main par defuer, et met igal.	and if the fracture is on the left side, place your index finger of the right hand, and gently press the fracture inwards, and stabilize it with the other hand from the outside, and make it even.
Et se li brisure de la mandibule est desevree en II, si covient que tu aministres extension de II pars, tant qu’il soit igalz.	And if the fracture of the jawbone is displaced in two parts, it is necessary to administer an extension of both sides until they are equal.
Et se commovemens des dens avient, ou routure, si les estrain d’un fil d’or ou d’argent ou de soie, puis met sus la mandibule brisie cerote, et met sus I drapel double;	And if the movement of teeth occurs, or they are dislocated, then extract them with a gold, silver, or silk thread, then place wax on the fractured jaw, and put two layers of cloth over it;
et met sus lou drapel une grant estele bien faite, ou une piece de cuir igal, longe et large selonc la mandibule, et la lie sus au mues que tu pues, et comande a malaide qu’il se repose, et menjuce viandes legieres.	and place on the cloth a large stake well made, or a piece of leather even, long and wide according to the mandible, and tie it up as high as you can, and instruct the patient to rest, and eat light foods.
Et se tu vois que li figure se chainge, si le deslie au tier jor, et puis remet a point ceu que c’est chaingiet;	And if you see that the appearance changes, then unbind on the third day, and then properly reset what has changed.
et met emplaustre sus, de la poudre dou moulin avec abun d’uef ou farine de sisament, aprés ceu que tu as osteit lou cerote;	and place a plaster on it, of the powder from the mill with plenty of egg or sesamum flour, after you have removed the wax.
et met sus l’emplaustre lainne legiere, et se li emplaustres s’aert, et li disposition dou malaide ne se chainge, laisse le tant k’il soit sanez;	and place light wool over the plaster, and if the condition of the patient does not change, leave it until he is well.
maintes fois est sanez en III semainnes.	Often recovery takes three weeks.
Et se apostemes chaus vient, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit maintes fois.	And if abscesses come, then treat them as we have said many times.
Et s’il i a brisure et plaie ensamble, rewarde se nule piece de l’os en est ostee;	And if there is a fracture and wound together, check if any piece of the bone has been removed;
si subtilie de l’oster as estrumens covenaubles a ceu.	use appropriate instruments to carefully remove it.
Et se li plaie est estroite, si l’eslarge a flaime selonc ta necessiteit.	And if the wound is narrow, then widen it with flame according to your necessity.
Et quant tu avras ostees toutes ces pieces, et il n’i demore nule, si cout la plaie, s’ele est large, et met sus I des emplaustres covenaubles a ceu, por enjanrer char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you have removed all these pieces and none remain, then close the wound if it is wide, and apply suitable plasters to it, to heal flesh until it is healthy.
de la forcele	Of the strength
Li forcele brise plusors fois devant, devers l’espaule, et li brisure si est selonc III manieres:	The collarbone is often broken multiple times near the shoulder, and the fracture occurs in three ways:
ou elle est brisie et desevree en II, et i a pieces, et est li plus legiere a restorer;	where it is broken and displaced into two parts with pieces remaining, and this is the easiest to restore;
ou il i a brisure avec plaie.	where there is a fracture with a wound.
Et li ovraiges si est quant li brisure est sens plaie, que tu aies II ministres, si que li uns teigne l’ajutoire que sent la forcele brisie;	And when the fracture is without a wound, you should have two assistants, so that one holds the shoulder which is connected to the broken collarbone;
et li autres estende lou col vers la partie;	and stretch the neck towards the affected part;
puis met igal la brisure a tes dois, si que li forme soit si com il covient, et n’i ait ne apparance ne chevement.	then align the fracture with your hands so that the form is as it should be, and there is no appearance or change.
Et se tu a mestier de plus estendre, si met desoz l’espaule au malaide une spere reonde de drap, ou de lainne, et soit grosse selonc ta necessiteit;	And if you need to stretch it further, place under the patient's shoulder a round ball of cloth, or wool, and let it be as large as necessary;
et estent et lieve la forcele, et estraint le spere a ta main, si que tu mettes igal la brisure, si com il covient.	and stretch and lift the muscle, and hold the ball with your hand so that you align the fracture as it should be.
Et se tu ne pues traire le chief de la forcele au defuer, por ceu qu’elle vient em parfont, si covient que li malaides gise sovin sus son hatereil, et met desoz l’espaule I oreillier moien, et boute li ministres l’espaule aval, tant que li os de la forcele soit levez.	And if you cannot draw the head of the humerus out due to its position, then the patient must lie supine on their back, and place a medium-sized pillow under the shoulder, and the assistant should push the shoulder down until the bone of the humerus is raised.
Et puis adrece la brisure a tes dois, et se tu lou trueves debrisiet, si covient que tu fendes sus;	And then set the fracture with your hands, and if you find it shattered, you must cut into it;
et trai fuer les pieces legierement, et se li os ne puet joindre por aucun sormontement, si le cope a l’un des incisoires que tu as;	and draw together the bones gently, and if the bone cannot join due to any prominence, cut it with one of the knives that you have;
mais que tu mettes desoz la forcele cest estrument, por warder lou syfac:	but place aside this instrument to protect the surface:
et semble une cuiller, et n’est mie chevez, et soit ausi large com il lou covient, selonc la grandor de l’os et la possance de l’uevre;	and it resembles a spoon, and is not sharp, and should be as wide as necessary, according to the size of the bone and the strength of the work;
et ait II chiés, si com tu vois, et soit li uns larges, et li autres estrois, si com est li routure de la plaie que tu as fait quant tu as trait les os;	and it should have two edges, as you see, one wide and the other narrow, like the shape of the wound you made when you treated the bones;
et quant tu es asseurez d’aposteme chaut, si cout la plaie, et se li routure est petite, ou tu doutes aposteme chaut, si emple la plaie de drapelz et de tentes, selonc sa quantiteit.	and when you are sure of a hot abscess, sew the wound shut, and if the wound is small where you suspect a hot abscess, dress the wound with cloths and bandages according to its size.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si moille I drapel en oile roset et en aisil et en vin, et met sus.	And if painful abscesses come, moisten a cloth in rose oil and egg yolk and wine, and apply it.
Li estrignement de l’os, quant il est sens plaies et sens tailleure, est que tu mettes sus l’os l’enplaustre de la poudre dou molin et d’aubun d’uef, et met estoupes legieres sus, et met une spere desoz l’assele, se tu en as mestier;	The binding of the bone, when it is without cuts and without incisions, is that you put on the bone the plaster made from powder from the mill and yolk of an egg, and place light wicks over it, and put a sphere beneath the bandage if you need to.
puis pren une tres grant bende d’une palme de large, puis met I drapeil double sus estoupes, et l’emplaustre;	Then take a very wide bandage of one palm in width, then place the wicks over the light cloths, and apply the plaster.
puis pren une estele subtil de III dois de large et de lonc, et l’envoloupe entor celui bendeil, si que li chief dou bendeil soient pendant;	Then take a fine strip three fingers wide and long, and wrap it around the bandage, so that the ends of the bandage hang down.
et met l’estele sus la briseure, et torne le bendeil sus lou col, et desoz l’asselle sainne, et desoz l’asselle malaide;	and place the strip over the fracture, and wrap the bandage around the neck, under the healthy shoulder, and under the injured shoulder.
et la ramoinne de chescune partie, et quant tu vois ke li lieure tient la briseure avenanment, et tu vois clerement que li estele ne se muet desus l’os brisiet, si le rewarde chescun jor, et quant li liiens eslaiche, si lou restraint;	And reset each part, and when you see that the ligament holds the fracture in place, and clearly see that the bone does not move above the broken bone, then treat it each day, and as the ligaments loosen, secure them.
et fai gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et li met quant il dort I petit orillier desoz l’assele, por lever l’ajutoire en haut;	And have the patient lie on his back, and place a small pillow under him while he sleeps to lift the shoulder up.
si aligera li brisure de la forcele par l’aligement de l’espaule, ou tu li lie lou bras au col, et ne lou desliier se malvais accidens n’i vient, jusc’a XX jors;	This will ease the fracture of the arm by aligning the shoulder, where you tie the arm to the neck, and do not untie it unless a bad accident occurs, until twenty days.
puis rencomence l’emplaustre, se tu vois qu’il en ait mestier, et l’estraint et le laisse ensi, tant qu’il soit restorez;	Then restart the poultice if you see it is needed, and bind it and leave it as such until he is restored.
et elle est restoree au plus en XXVIII jors, et en moins a aucuns homes.	and it is restored in twenty-eight days, and in fewer days for some men.
de la brisure de l’espaule	of the fracture of the shoulder
Poc avient que li espaule brise ou large leu ne em mileu, et ne lou seit on fuers que par lou touchement;	It rarely happens that the shoulder is broken either widely or in the middle, and one can only know this by touching it;
si l’apareille selonc la figure de la brisure, et la ramoinne selonc sa forme natureil, en toutes les manieres que tu pues;	if you set it according to the shape of the break, and reset it according to its natural form, in all ways that you can;
puis met sor le leu poudre dou molin avec abun d’uef, et estoupes legieres, et met sus I drapeil double;	then place powder from the mill with an abundance of egg, and use light dressings, and put on one double cloth;
puis met sus une estele large et subtil, un poc plus large de l’espaule, et se desoz l’estele est chevemens en aucun leu de l’espaule, si emple celle cheveure d’estoupes de lin, si que li estele siece igalment;	then place a wide and fine board over it, slightly wider than the shoulder, and if any part of the board presses on the shoulder, pad that area with linen dressings so that the board rests evenly;
et puis l’estraint a tout une grant bende fermement, si que li estele ne se mueve de son leu, et regarde le liien chescun jor;	and then tightly bind it with a large bandage so that the bone does not move from its place, and examine the joint each day;
et toutes les fois k’il amolist, si l’estraint, et met igal l’estele s’elle est fuer de son leu, et gise li malaides sus son costeit;	and every time it softens, bind it again, and place the bone back in its proper position if it has moved out of place, and have the patient lie on their side;
et li espaule est restouree en XX jors ou en XXV.	and the shoulder is reset in twenty days or twenty-five.
Et quant cist nombres est acomplis, si le deslie, et soies seur, car ce n’est mie os qui se mette fuer legierement.	And when this number of days is complete, then release it, and be careful, for this is not a bone that easily returns to its proper place.
Et se une piece de l’os tent avant, et point desoz lou keur, si fent sus, et l’oste, et fai ceu que nos avons dit en la brisure de la forcele d’apaisier aposteme chaut.	And if a piece of the bone protrudes and sticks out from near the heart, cut it off, and do as we have said regarding the fracture to alleviate a hot abscess.
de la brisure dou pis	of the fracture of the foot
Li peis est aucune fois brisiez em mileu, mais ce avient poc;	The foot is sometimes broken in the middle, but this happens rarely;
mais il brise sovent au defuer.	but it often breaks upon removal.
Et quant il est brisiez emmi, si decline au desoz, et sent li malaides grant dolor, et faute d’alainne, et toust, et par aventure vomist sanc, et apert li chevemens en l’os brisiés, et lou sent om bien.	And when it is fractured in the middle, it tilts outward, and the patient feels great pain, and lacks alignment, and swells, and sometimes vomits blood, and the movement of the bone can be felt through the skin.
Et li restoracion si est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos, et li met I cussin entre les espaules, puis presse les espaules, et li assemble les costes des II costelz a tes mains, et subtilie dou mettre igal a toutes les manieres que tu pues, tant que li figure de l’os soit si com il covient;	And the restoration is such that the patient lies supine on their back, and places a cushion between the shoulders, then presses the shoulders, and brings together the sides of the two shoulder blades with his hands, and gently aligns them equally in all ways that he can, until the shape of the bone is as it should be;
puis met sus emplaustres et estoupes desus l’estele subtil de salz, ou d’autre fust legier, et l’envoloupe en I drapeil, et la lie sus l’os brisiet, si qu’elle ne se mueve;	then applies plasters and inserts a light stick wrapped in salt, or another light material, above the fracture gently, and wraps it around the broken bone so that it does not move;
et torne le liien reondement au dos, et l’estraint avenanment, et rewarde chescune houre la liure, et s’elle ramolist, si l’estraint;	and wraps the bandage smoothly around the back, and tightens it gradually, and checks each hour the wrapping, and if it loosens, then tighten it;
et s’il lou covient desliier, por corrosion ou por prurite que vient au leu, ou dolor ou aposteme, si te haste, et lou deslie, et raie l’emplaustre, et adresce ceu qui i est venus de manieres de cures;	And if it needs to be loosened, for corrosion or itching that comes to the area, or pain or abscess, then hurry and loosen it, and scrape off the plaster, and address what has come from treatments in various ways;
puis ramoinne l’emplaustre, et l’estraint tant qu’il soit sanez.	then reapply the plaster, and press it until it is secure.
de la brisure des costes	Of the fracture of the ribs
Saiches que li briseure des costes ne vient fuer que en leus gros aprés le dos, et au chief dedens, et ne ploient fuer que por ceu qu’eles sont glairouses;	Know that the breaker of ribs does not cause pain except in their large parts behind the back and at the front, and they only hurt because they are bruised;
et le sent om bien a l’inquisition as dois.	and one feels it well during examination of the back.
Et li restoremens si est que tu met igal la brisure, si com il covient.	And the restoration is that you place the fracture evenly as it should be.
Et puis met l’emplaustre, et l’estraint d’une estele, se tu en as mestier.	And then apply the plaster, and bind it with a bandage if you need to.
Et se li brisure des costes est declinans au dedens, si sent li malaides tres grant dolor, et pointure, ausi com de pleuresin, car li os point la toile;	And if the break of the ribs is inwardly displaced, then the patient feels great pain and piercing, as with pleurisy, because the bone pierces the tissue;
et alaine a poinnes, et toust et vomist grant planteit de sanc, et c’est de grief santeit, et li ancien i ont mis grant engien.	And he spits out points, and soon vomits great quantities of blood, and this is from severe illness, and the elderly have much fear about it.
Et si a de ces qui dient qu’il le covient aministrer viandes qui enflent le ventre, por bouter la briseure au defuer.	And there are those who say that it is necessary to administer foods that swell the belly, to push the fracture outwards.
Nos ne faisons mie ceu, que apostemes chaulz n’i viegne, s’il n’i est venus.	We do not do this, that abscesses may not come, if they have already come.
Et s’il i est venus, si le saine.	And if they have come, then heal them.
Et dirent aucun d’ous c’on met ventouses sor le leu, por sucier forment, et c’est semblant a raison;	And some say that one should place suction cups on the area to suck strongly, and this seems reasonable;
toutevoie, doutance i a que li ventouse n’atraie les superfluitez au leu por la disposition de foiblece.	nevertheless, there is concern that the suction cups may not draw the excesses to the area due to the disposition of weakness.
Et dirent aucun d’ous c’on doit covrir le leu de lainne moillie en oile chaut, et met on tentes entre les costes por metre igal la lieure entor, puis soit curez de la cure de pleurisin, de viande et de medicine.	And some say that one should cover the area with wool soaked in hot oil, and place tents between the ribs to evenly distribute the poultice, then treat it according to the treatment for pleurisy, with food and medicine.
Et se li malaides sent grant dolor qu’il ne puet soffrir par l’os qui point la toile, et doutance est au malaide, si covient fendre sus lou leu de la coste brisie, et covient mettre desoz I estrument por warder lou syfac;	And if the patient feels great pain that they cannot bear from the bone piercing the skin, and there is doubt for the patient, then it is necessary to cut into the area of the broken rib, and an instrument must be placed underneath to protect the surface;
et adonques doit on trenchier l’os, et traire legierement, et puis coudre les II levres de la plaie, s’elle est grans, et le curez d’emplaustres, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And then one must cut the bone, and gently scrape it, and then sew together the two edges of the wound, if it is large, and treat it with plasters until it is healed.
Et se apostemes chaus vient, si met sus drapelz moilliez en oile roset, et met sus lou leu;	And if pus-filled abscesses come, place strips moistened in rose oil on them, and apply them to the area.
et cure tandis le leu de ceu qu’il covient a aposteme, et soit gisans sovins sus lou costeit ou il doit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	and treat the area as is appropriate for an abscess, and let them lie on their side on the side where it is necessary, until they are healed.
de la brisure dou col	of the fracture of the neck (or collarbone)
Aucune fois vient briseure as os dou col, et poc avient k’il ploie;	Sometimes there is a fracture in the neck bones, and it can happen that they bend.
et ausi a l’espinee dou dos.	and similarly to the spine of the back.
Et quant ce avient a aucun, et tu vues savoir s’il sera sanez ou non, si pren warde se tu vois ses mains mollifiies et enflees et mortes, et ne les puet movoir ne estendre, et quant tu les poins d’une aguille, si ne lou sent.	And when this happens to someone, and you wish to know if they will be well or not, observe if you see their hands soft, swollen, and dead-colored, and cannot move or stretch them, and when you prick them with a needle, they do not feel it.
Saiches qu’il est mortelz em plusors dispositions, et s’il les muet et sent bien quant on les estraint et point, saiches que li jointure de l’os est sauve, et que li malaides iert curez, s’on i met cure.	Know that it is mortal in many cases, and if they move and feel well when you pinch and prick them, know that the joint of the bone is safe, and that the patient can be treated, if proper care is applied.
Et se semblans chose vient a l’espinee dou dos, et tu vues savoir s’il iert sanez ou non, si pren warde se li piez sont amollis, et se li accident i sont qui sont em mains, et sus lou dos saut ventositeit et egestion sens volonteit;	And if a similar thing happens to the spine of the back, and you wish to know whether it is sound or not, observe if the feet are weak, and see if there are signs that can be felt by hand, and on the back feel for windiness and involuntary evacuation;
et quant on l’a sovineit sus son ventre, si saut egestion sens volonteit.	and when it is pressed upon its belly, there is involuntary evacuation.
Et quant il est sovinez sus son dos et il vuet asseller, si ne puet.	And when he is lying on his back and wants to sit up, he cannot.
Saiches qu’il est mortelz:	Know that it is fatal:
si ne laboreir mie en sa cure.	do not attempt to treat it.
Et se cist accident ne li vienent, si est li chose plus legiere.	And if these accidents do not occur to him, then the matter is lighter.
Et li cure si est que tu rewardes s’il i a aposteme chaut, si met sus l’espinee oile roset ou oile de moieuf d’uef, tant qu’il soit apaisiez;	And the treatment is that you observe if there is a hot abscess, then apply rose oil or chicken egg yolk to the spine until it subsides;
puis met sus un des emplaustres confortans et sechans, et le lie d’un liien, et comande au malaide a reposer;	Then apply one of the comforting and drying plasters, and bind it with a bandage, and instruct the patient to rest;
et ne dorme mie sus celle partie ou il sent la dolor, tant k’il soit sanez.	and do not let them sleep on that part where they feel the pain, until they are healed.
Et se aucuns os se dessevre, si covient coper sus lou keur;	And if any bone breaks, it is necessary to cut into the chest;
et oste l’os, puis assemble les II levres de la plaie, s’elle est grans, a une costure, puis le cure d’oignement enjanrant char, tant qu’il soit sanez;	and remove the bone, then stitch together the two edges of the wound if it is large, and treat it with an ointment that promotes flesh growth until they are healed;
et se li chiés de l’os est brisiez, ki est apelez li «chiés de la kowe», se i boute ton pouchet de ta main senestre, et le met igal a l’autre main a ton pooir, puis met l’emplaustre et l’estele sus, se tu en a mestier;	and if the head of the bone is broken, which is called the "head of the wrist," place your thumb from your left hand there and align it as best you can with your right hand, then apply the plaster and bandage, if necessary;
puis l’estraint, et s’il i a os desevreit, si fent sus, et l’oste, et cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit sanee.	Then it is extracted, and if there are displaced bones, they cut them out, and treat the wound until it is healed.
de la brisure de l’os de la hainche	Of the fracture of the hip bone
Poc avient que li os de la hainche soit brisiez, et s’il avient, si n’avient fuer c’un poc d’amenuisement au chief;	It sometimes happens that the hip bone is broken, and if it does happen, there is often only a slight concussion to the head;
et fent dou lonc, et decline au pardedens, et vient au malaide dolor au leu, et pointure, et enfle ceu que brise.	and they cut it long, and it declines inwardly, and causes pain to the patient at the site, and stiffness, and swelling where it is broken.
Et li restoration si est que tu estendes ta main sus, tant que tu soies sus la briseure;	And the restoration is that you extend your hand above it, until you are above the break;
et saiches quelz est li brisure et li figure de li;	and identify where the fracture is and its shape;
et se li brisure est au chief soulement, si met igal cele brisure, tant qu’ele soit a figure natureil.	And if the fracture is to the head alone, set it equal so that it has a natural shape.
Et se li brisure est dou lonc, ou elle decline au dedens, si fai gesir le malaide sus son ventre, tant que li restauration de cele brisure te soit aparillie.	And if the fracture extends along its length and tilts inward, make the patient lie on their stomach until the restoration of that fracture is prepared.
Et quant tu l’avras mise igal, si met sus l’emplaustre, puis met sus une estele de fust ou de keur, et estraint la briseure, si qu’ele ne se mueve;	And when you have set it equal, apply a plaster, then place a splint of wood or horn, and bind the fracture so that it does not move;
et emple le leu desoz les costes, tant que li lieure soit igalz.	and support the area below the ribs, so that the sides are even.
Et comande au malaide k’il dorme sus son costeit sain, ou sus son dos.	And instruct the patient to sleep on their healthy side or on their back.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si n’i tochier, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et met sus ceu que nos avons devant dit;	And if there is inflammation present, do not touch it, until the inflammation subsides, and then apply what we have mentioned before;
et puis revien a la restauration, et l’estraint si com il covient, s’il n’i a nul mavais accident;	and then return to the restoration, and bind it as is appropriate, if there is no harmful incident;
et c’est li maniere.	And this is the manner.
de la brisure de l’ajutoire	of the fracture of the shoulder
Li adjutoires est ceu qui est entre lou coute et lou chief de l’espaule, et s’il est brisiez, si le doit on restorer selonc l’une des II manieres:	The shoulder joint is what is between the collarbone and the head of the shoulder, and if it is broken, one must restore it according to one of the two methods:
dont l’une est que tu pren I fust plain de moiene groissor, selonc ceste forme:	one of which is that you take one staff filled with medicinal material, in this form:
Et lie as II chiés II liens, et les pent en haut, et siece li malaide sus I siege;	And tie the two heads with two straps, and pull them up, and seat the patient on a chair;
